LETTER OF TRANSMISSION
To: President, Korea Gas Corporation
Dear Sir,
We hereby submit "Environmental Impact Assessment for 2nd LNG Receiving
Terminal Construction Project" as a final report, which has come to an agree-
ment at Oct. 8, 1990.
October, 1991
Jung-Kyu Yu, P.E
President
Yooshin Engineering Corporation

CHAPTER 1.
INTRODUCTION
-1-






CHAPTER 1. Introduction
1.1 General
For continuous economic development of our country, it is required to
sustain stable supply and variety of energy sources for a long term basis,
however, supply and demand of oil is becoming unstable day by day.
Accordingly, government have decided to establish Korea Gas Corporation and
place a contract to import LNG ( Liquefied Natural Gas ) from Indonesia for
a period of 1986 to 2006 at Pyung-taek LNG receiving terminal.
Furthermore, the Ministry of Environment has laid down a law to use
city gas or low sulfur oil, which are clean energy, about the heat    supply
facilities for office, business and supply of Seoul city as of Sep. 1, 1988
to mitigate the gradual aggravation of  air   quality  and  is planning   to
expand target area to the whole area of Seoul and Metropolitan area.
In the light of above tendency, it is decided to construct Incheon
LNG  receiving  terminal at    Incheon  common water to    supply  LNG   for
metropolitan area gently and detailed descriptions are as follows.
-  Title of the project      INCHEON LNG   receiving  terminal  construction
project
-  Location : Tidal land which is 7 km far away from southern area of   Song
do,Nam ku, Incheon city
-  Area    990,000nt ( 825 m X 1200 m)
-  Owner   Korea Gas Corporation
1.2 Major Elements Affect Environment
It is anticipated that Incheon LNG receiving terminal construction
project may cause change of topography, marine ecosystem and marine
environment etc., as impacts of natural environment and impacts of living
environment such as air quality, noise, seawater quality under construction
of the project.
1.2.1 Natural Environment
-  For entrance channel of LNG tank carrier,    11,859,000 md   of  dredging
work and 7.5 km of causeway and 990,000 e site preparation for the project
is required and thus, it is expected that change of marine ecosystem and
natural topography could be happened.
- 3-



- Tides, tidal discharge, current velocity and sedimentation will be
changed according to causeway, receiving terminal and entrance channel
construction as follows.
* Tides - Tidal range will be decreased by 5 cm ( 0.6 % ) as reclamate
the project site, because seawater level will be raised by 1 cm and 4 cm at
low tide and at high tide respectively in front of LNG receiving terminal
site comparing to present state.
*   Tidal  discharge - Mean tidal     discharge  due to the     project
construction will become from 3,593 X 106 m' to 109 X 106 nt , thus,
decreased by 3 %.
* In marine ecosystem, Phytoplankton is 156 species and their primary
productivity ranges of 141.5 - 693.8 ml/d .day, and standing crop of
Zooplankkton is 1,106 - 26,033 Inds/ni as 4 classified groups.
Predominant animal group in Benthos is Polychaeta and distribution range of
Microorganism is revealed as 1 X 10 cells/ml - 3 X 106 cells/ml and is
shown in the order of summer, spring, winter and autumn.
As an impacts on marine ecosystem due to project construction, species and
quantity reduction of    eggs, young fishes,    plankton  and  Benthos are
expected and the catch of shellfish is also expected to be reduced, since
shellfish is affected by sedimentation and reclamation rather than impact
of SS.
1.2.2 Living Environment
- The project site, tidal land at front sea of Song do, is located near at
the site to be prepared by reclamation for new marine city of Song do and
990,000 m of LNG receiving terminal site, 1 Berth of Marine facilities,
2,000 m of Trestle, 8,500 m of sea-route channel including 700 m for vessel
turning area and 7.5 km of causeway ( 8 m width ) will be built for this
project.
- It is investigated that observed value of air quality at tidal land is
within the environmental limit and transient impact on the air quality by
vehicle under construction is anticipated.
- Seawater quality investigation has been resulted as 3.6 mg/l of ODD,
25.3 mg/l of SS and impacts described as below are expected to be exist
either by reclamation and dredging under the process of construction or by
discharge of sewage of 300 operational personel under operation of
receiving terminal.
-4 -



* Under the process of construction
Based on the prediction results of SS concentration, area where SS
concentration revealed to increase over 1 ppm is 144.4 7d and 109.3 e at
flood tide and at ebb tide respectively.
* Under the operation of receiving terminal
It is predicted that the quantity of sewage is 16.5 ne/day and load
quantity of COD is 2.8 kg/day, thus, COD will be increased not more than
0.01 ppm at the front of outlet when disposed without treatment.
1.3 Methods for Reducing the Baneful Impacts
- Install Filter mat to avoid damage of facilities in the process of
revetment construction.
- To mitigate air pollution. temporarilly during construction, improve
project work control and install dust protection curtain and washing
facilities for vehicle and vehicle tire in front of causeway.
- To prevent seawater from pollution, install Silt protector to restraint
the production of suspended solid at the place performing reclamation and
dredging work under the construction stage, and operate sewage treatment
system  which  adopt  Contact  Stabilization   Process   to   sustain   BOD
concentration of discharge below 30 mg/l under receiving terminal operation
stage, and provide Oil fence for the unexpected accident of LNG tank
carrier.
- To decrease noise level, have the construction vehicle in low speed
service and limit night time work during construction stage.
- After the completion of the project facilities, prepare a perfect fire
fighting system for any case of emergency.
1.4   Plans for the Environmental Management After Construction
For environment management plan due to Incheon LNG receiving
terminal construction project, assurance should be made by that performance
to  investigate marine   ecosystem  seasonally,  inspect   silt   protector
condition at the reclamation and dredging work area frequently for seawater
quality and invetigation should be carried out monyhly basis on 5 stations
near project site.
Also it is requested to establish a fire-fighting system against the
efflux of LNG for health and safety plan.
- 5 -



1.5 Alternatives
Three proposed site, Yul island area, Young-jong island area and
front sea of Song island, has been analyzed about entrance channel and
harbour condition,connectivity and topographical condition taking due
consideration of conditions of each location and the result indicates that
front sea of Song island is concluded as the best location for vessel
transportation and decided as project site.
1.6 Conclusion
The project site is located at the front sea of Song island, Nam ku,
Incheon city and formed by tidal land and close to proposed site for future
new marine city of Song island.   Several type of environmetal  impacts  by
Inchoen LNG receiving terminal project will be expected to be produced,
however, the impacts are negligible as prescribed above and pleasant
environment can be accomplished by establishment of continuous monitoring
system on environment preservation and mitigation of environmental impacts.
Furthermore, reasonable and effective management plan  is established
and operated for least impacts and unavoidable impacts which are to be
produced during reclamation works and thus, not only coincide the purpose
of the project but also perform a part of environment preservation by doing
best effort not to affect project site and it's circumferencial area.
On the other hands, the project will also contribute to air quality
improvement of metropolitan district by supplying clean energy LNG to
metropolitan district.
-6-



CHAPTER 2.
PROJECT DESCRIPTION
- 7 -






CHAPTER 2 Project Description
2.1 Background and Purpose of Project
Since industrialization of our country is carried out by oil industry
as central figure,   thus the demand of oil is continuously increasing   and
however, supply and price of oil are in a very precarious state because
most of oil producing countries are concentrated at Middle East where is
unstable politically and an predicted amount of oil deposit is assumed to
be used approximately for next 30 years only.       Particularly,  Gulf  war
have made the political state of Middle East more unstable and therefore,
serious impacts such as skyrocketing of oil price etc, has brought energy
crisis to domestic industries.
In the meanwhile, LNG is being produced at the several dispersed
places of the world and predicted amount of deposit is more abundant than
oil  and  hence,  steady   supply  of  LNG  is   guaranteed   comparatively.
Therefore, it has been planned to construct Incheon LNG receiving terminal
site to make a preparation for environment control and newly required
demand on power generation of municipal area according to the construction
of thermoelectric power plant at Yil island, Incheon, and sudden increase
of demand on city gas according to new city development.
And  hence,   as  a  provision  described  above,   reduction  of  air
pollution for municipal area by the expanded supply of natural gas,
convenient & easy life due to gas usage and shrink of oil dependence by
diversity of energy sources are to be expected after completion of the
project.
2.2 Performance Details and Plan of the Project
The project is being carried out based on the national LNG supply
plan by the government and the project plan to be performed should be
discussed and cooperated with the Ministry    of  Construction,   the  Korea
Maritime and Port Administration, Incheon city, the Office of National
Fisheries Administration and Military Forces etc., and an approval of the
Office of Environment and the Ministry of Construction shall be obtained on
the  environmental   impact  assessment  and  procedure  for  approval   and
cooperation are presented at Fig. 2.2 - 1 & 2.
- 9

Chapter     3.  GeneraR Site       Condition
3.1 Geographical Location of the Project site
Incheon city to where the project site helongs is adjoining to west
coast of central district of korea peninsula and is located at the place
where, Long. 1260 47' 12" - 1260 33' 30" E and N.L. 370 22' 24" -   370  35'
00", is 42 km west far from capital Seoul.     Incheon city,  as an  harbour
city which takes a role of marine gate   for a   national  capital,   has  a
sinusoidal coastline and inner port is prevented by Wol-mi island and
So-wol-mi island and outer port is surrounded by several islands such as
Young-jong island, Yong-you island, Young-heung island, Deuk-jeuk island
etc., as well and therefore, it is an international harbour fulfilling
modern facilities.

On the other hands,   the project site is located at the   tidal  land
of the sea, Long. 1260 36' and N.L. 370 22', where is 7.0 km far from
southern area of Song island, Nam ku, Incheon city.
3.2 Environmental Condition of the Project Site
For environmental condition evaluation of the project site, districts
related environment such as partial area of Kyung-ki do, Shi-heung city,
Hwa-seung goon, Ansan city centering Incheon city and the facilities induce
environmental damage such as district designation, railways and object to
be conserved such as a natural monument, cultural properties, a fishery
right and basic environmental protection facilities like sewage treatment
system, wastes landfill area and development planning specifies on the
basic development planning of Incheon city have been investigated.

CHAPTER 4. Comparative Diagraw Between Enviromnental
Factors and Environmental Factors
4.1 Preparation of Environmental Impact Assessment
Preparation of   environmental  impact  assessment    is proceeded   as
depicted in Fig. 4.1 - 1 and prediction on the report is normally carried
out at the point of time that project plan take concrete shape to a some
extent ( basic design stage ) by settling basic plan even its term is
variable according to its specialty though.
Looking into the preparation procedure of environmental impact
assessment report step by step, first of all, derive environmental impact
element and factor due to the performance of the project after acquaintance
of planning and project characteristics and, investigate and understand
environment status of the project site through site survey, environmental
quality investigation, information collection etc.
Secondary, by gathering the results of site survey and data collection
of related project, impact prediction should be made by establishment of
prediction criterior and adjustment of prediction item.
Thus, baneful impact mitigation method and countermeasures, derivation
of  unavoidable    impacts   and   consideration    of   alternatives,   post
environmental management plan shall be set up based on above results.

4.2 Characteristics of the Project
- Possess plane tidal lands.
- Provide 1,200 m X 825 m site by reclamation at the front sea where is
located 7.8 km far from Song do, Incheon.
- Contruction steps are denoted as reclamatioxn works like terminal site
preparation, causeway construction and dredging works of entrance channel
from the channel of Incheon harbour.
- Expansion of LNG supply will contribute to air quality improvement of
municipal area remarkably after the completion of terminal construction.
4.3 Derivation of Environmental Impact Factor
Environmental impact factor means the major sources that can take
place impacts on the environment of project site and circumferencial area
according to development plan and environmental impact elements of Incheon
LNG receiving terminal construction project are as follows.
4.3.1 Construction Stage
- Alteration of natural topography
* change of shore line, seabed and change of tidal land
- Collection and transportation of construction material
* pebbles collection, stone collection and instrument material
transportation
- Constructions
* dredging, reclamation, concrete placing, pavement, pile driving,
revetment, commitment of construction manpower
4.3.2 Operation Stage
- Existence of the structure
* quay wall, revetment, mooring facilities, reserve and unloading
equipments, building, roads
-33-



4.4 Matrix comparison of Environmental Impact Factors
4.4.1 Set-up of Items to be Investigated
Bad smells and sunshine disturbances in the fields of living
environment are excluded from the items to be investigated, since no
impacts are assumed to be occurred taking due consideration of site
condition and project characteristics.
(Table 4.4.1-1)   Set-Up of Items to be investigated for Environmental Impact
- Climate ;   No alteration of climate due to Incheon LNG receiving  terminal
construction project is anticipated, however, it is required to understand
the present state of weather condition and utilize for basic data about
other items to be estimated.
- Topography & Geology   ;    Topographical  and Geological   change  due  to
reclamation and sedimentation is expected and thus, this will be used for
reference when impact prediction and mitigation method are established.
- Ecosystem ;   Grasp distribution of the Pisces and devise mitigation method
for damage on ecosystem under construction
- Marine environment ;    Establish mitigation   method on   the  impacts  by
sedimentation etc, considering physical properties of tides around project
site.
- Natural resources i   Forecast the alteration trend of natural resources
after construction.
- Land utility ;   Investigate the present state such as general condition of
land utillity and predict impacts as the purpose of land utility owing to
this project changes.
- Air quality ;   Predict the air quality    change  under  construction  and
operation of LNG receiving terminal by grasping the status of air
pollution.
- Water environment ;   Predict pollution increase of   solids  and floating
materials because of dredging and reclamation at construction stage and
alteration of water quality pollution degree by efflux of sewage.
- Land pollution i   Grasp the status of land pollution degree at the area to
be affected.
- Wastes ;   Consider production of living wastes and appropriate   treatment
under operation.
-34-



- Noise ;   Predict impacts to be occured by the operation of    construction
equipment at the circumferencial area considering characteristics and size
of the project and general condition of the district.
- Jamming ;   Establish  countermeasures  on the   impacts of   eletric  wave
jamming due to the project construction.
- Leisure & Scenery ;   Review on the connection to near leisure facilities.
- Public health i   Consider public health by the  project  construction  and
water supply.
- Population & habitation i   Grasp the present state of population  at  near
area of project site and utilize above for basic data to predict impacts
due to the project construction.
- Industries ;   Utilize for  basic  data  to  estimate  the possibility   of
connection by grasping of the status of industries around project site.
- Public facilities ;   Utilize for basic data by grasping public  facilities
around project site.
- Transportation i    Predict  impacts according   to traffic   increase  and
traffic  system change   around the project site due to       the   project
construction.
- Education ;   Grasp the   existence of   education facilities   around  the
project site.
- Cultural properties ;   Grasp the existence of cultural  properties  around
the project site.
-35-

CHAPTER 5. Present Envrionmental Conditions,
Environmental Impacts by Project, Methods
for Reducing the Baneful Impacts
5. 1. Natural Environment
5. 1. 1 Meteorology
A. The Present Environmental Condition
Since   Incheon   is   located    at   central     west    coast    area
geographically, the   weather   in  Incheon   is   very   dry  and    cold   in
winter, hot   and   humid    in   summer   due    to   the   continental   high
pressure.
Therefore,   weather  condition   for  site  has   been  collected    from
the  data   of  Incheon  meteorological   station using   a   past    decade  (
1980 - 1989 ),   considering   that the  site   is  at  the  shore   area    of
Incheon.   The  location  of   the  Incheon  meteorological    station   is  as
follows.
(Table 5.1.1-1) Location of Meteorological Station
Location    North     East        H (m)      Hb (m)    ht (m)    ha (m)   hr (m)
Latitude longitude
Incheon     3712911  126'38"      68.9        70.4      1.4       14.0      0.2
* Note:   H  : height of ground above C.D
Hb : height of barometer
ht : height of thermometer from ground
hr : height of flow meter from ground
ha : height of anemometer from ground
Survey   results  from  the   data  during  a  decade   ( 1980   -1989   )
shows  that   the  average   temperature,  rainfall, evaporation    and    wind
speed  are   11.4 oc,  1088.3 mm,   1200.3 mm and    3.4  m/sec   respectively
as in the table 5. 1. 1 - 2 and Fig. 5. 1. 1 - 1.

1. Temperature
Since   the   project   site   is   governed   by    the    classical
continental  high pressure,   the annual   difference  in temperature    is
43.5 'c .   In other    words,   the   average    lowest   temperature   in
winter  is  -12.0 °c , very cold and dry     whereas  the average   highest
temperature in summer is 31.5°c , very hot and humid.
The  seasonal  average  temperatures  are  10.2°c  for  spring,   23.0
C   for   summer,    13.9 'C   for   autumn   and   -1.5 °C   for   winter
respectively  which have   been  shown on   table  5. 1. 1 - 3.    In   the
meanwhile,  average  temperature  in the most hot    and cold    month   is
24.8 °C in August and    -1.4 °c in January.
(Table 5.1.1-3)          Seasonal average temperature
(Unit:°C)
Season          Spring        Summer         Autumn        Winter
Incheon          10.2           23.0           13.9          -1.5
* reference : CMO Annual Meteorological Report(1980 - 1989)
2. Relative   Humidity
Relative humidity of project      site   is   70 %    which   is   very
optimal  for  daily  life.  The  lowest humidity   which mainly   exist  in
late winter or spring ( JAN. or FEB. ) is 63 %, whereas the highest
humidity  is 82 % ( Jul. ) and therefore higher      humidity   present  at
summer season rather than winter season.

3. Rainfall
Yearly  average   rainfall  of  the   project  site  is 1088.3 mm    which
is less than that of inland area, Seoul (1169.5 mm ). The monthly
maximum rainfall ( 283.2 mm ) is occurred at July and more than a
half of annual rainfall amount is concentrated at summer season.
Above phenomenon is presummed due to the seasonal rain front and
typhoon which are caused by the combination of hot and humid
northern Pacific air mass which moves towards north and cold air
mass of Okhotsk Sea. This specific characteristic of rainfall is
observed at the whole area of this country. Seasonal rainfall
variation of project site is shown at table 5. 1. 1 - 5.
(Table 5.1.1-5)           Seasonal rainfall variation

5. Wind Direction and Wind Speed.
Annual Meteorological Report    for   a   decade  ( 1980 -    1989  )
indicates that yearly    average wind speed   at the project site     and
circumferencial area   is 3.4 m/sec which   is very  severe and    monthly
average max. wind speed     is 4.0 m/sec mainly  in February   and   March
and  monthy average min, wind speed     is 2.7 m/sec  in September.
Wind Rose Map using   percent wind direction   and max. wind    speed
is  shown  at Fig. 5. 1. 1 - 3      and   gives   the   points that    the
seasonal governing   wind directions  are SSW   in spring & summer     and
NNE  in  autumn and winter. Maximun wind     speed   and   direction   are
16.7 m/sec and NW respectively within this period.

6.  Evaporation
The   amount    of   evaporation   is   affected    mainly    due    to
temperature,   humidity,  sunshine  duration   and  wind   speed   etc,   and
observed yearly amount of evaporation of this site area is 1200.3
mm.  In   summer,  a third  of  them   is  evaporated  and  monthly   average
max. and    min.  evaporation  is  148.1 mm   in   June   and   41.6  mm    in
January. In    the  meanwhile,  evaporation more than 100 mm    is   occurred
during  April   to  September  and  evaporation less than 50 mm   is   during
October to March.

5. 1. 2. Topography and Geology
A. The Present Environmental Condition
1. Topography
Incheon is located at the central west coast area of the Korea
Peninsula about 42 km away west from Seoul, in between 126o 47' 12"
- 126o 33' 30"  of  east  longitude  and   370 22' 24"  -  370  35' 00"  of
north latitude. Incheon is a international harbour city performing a
role of   the marine entrance    of   capital  Seoul   and   has   a   very
complicated  shore  line.  Moreover,  the  variation of   tidal  range   is
so high and Wol-mi   island and   small  Wol - mi    island   is   crossing
-53-



near the   inner   harbour   of   Incheon   whereas,   outer   harbour   is
surrounded by   several  island such   as Young-jong, Young -you,    Young-
heung and Deuck-juck island.
Geologically,  project site   is situated   in   the   front  sea   of
Incheon city, composed of the senesecent geology, Hasami Mt.(140 m)
& 0-bong  Mt.(106 m) besides   So-rea Mt.(299   m) are    declined towards
the southwest of the project site.
Basically, project   site  is not   adequate for harbour since     the
inclination   is   quite   gentle   and   tidal   ranges   are   so   high.
Characteristics of the submarine topography at the project site are
that the   reclaimed  land  spreaded out around the coastal       area   of
islands at an low water level, and the other area except reclaimed
land  forms   the   main water way    from   Pal-mi   island   to   Incheon
harbour. Water depth is intended to deeper towards the outer harbour
and main   transportation  way from the northwest of Pal-       mi   island
to the coastal part constitutes around 20 m wather depth.
Because  compatible  strong  tidal flows(2-3 km) are     being  shaped
around this   area,  sand bar which    develops  very frequently  such   an
above  area  spreaded  out northeast    to  southwest   at   the   northern
area  of  Pal- mi  island.          Sometimes,  sea valley can  be   formed
along the direcion of    tidal  current,  therefore  tides would be     the
major element to affect the submarine topography.
On  the other hand,    sea  area  around  the project   site  is   the
part  of  Kyoung-ki bay, surrounded    by  the  several kinds   of   island
and tidal ranges are big and wide along the coastline.
-54-

a) Description of Geology.
The  stratum of project site      are   composed   of   the  part   of
gneiss  which  mainly  are combined    gneiss,  etc   and   the   part   of
schist. Generally,  these  gneiss have  shown  a clear   structure of   the
gneiss even  the shape and structure   in gneiss   is different   according
to the amount and the composition of minerals in it though, and these
are generated by the weathering to the schist.
The  schists  are   composed   of  micaschists   mainly   and partial
quartz schists which are metamorphic sedimentary rocks, however, the
difference of micaschist and quartz schist is based on the amount of
mica and quartz respectively.
All  others  are  smaller  depth of   acid  rock   which  is composed    of
quartzite and felsite and base rock as a porphyry.
An alluvium is covered irregularly on the wider based rock as
gneiss and  rubble,  sand,  silty  clay,  small amount  of   organics   are
still remains not in solid.
b) Description of Soil Stratum.
Sedimentation characteristic  of west coast area  in our country    is
variable  based on the   change  in a sea    level   and the    supply   of
materials to be accumulated.
Horizontal distance of shore line at spring and neap tide which varies
approximately  8 - 9 m  is more    than   even   lOkm   in   some   places.
Accordingly,  wide & even  lake and diverse passing ways are formed      by
natural and reclaimed lands are developed extensively.
Base rock of this project site is composed of gneiss group as the
metamorphic  rock of   Gyung-gi  gneiss complex.   Weathered   rock   layor
which  formed  by weathering   for a long time  exist   forming   extensive
at an upper layer of base rock and then accumulation layers are exist
forming extensive and even current stream.
In conclusion, soil strata of the project site are coustructed
on the order of accumulation layer, weathered layer and base rock
layer and the description of each layer are as follows.

(1) Accumulation Layer
(a) LNG Receiving Terminal Area.
Above  area  is  composed    of   sandy   silt  layer,   silty   clay
layer, silty sand and still accumulated on it. The layer of sandy
silt is mostly in grey colour and brown or grey brown colour, 1.9
m - 13.5 m   thick, and N-value from  standard penetration  test  has    been
ranged about 5 - 36 / 30 cm diversely. Silty clay which mostly occupy
at  the  lower   layer of  sandy  silt  stratum  is   in   brown   to    grey
color, 2.3 - 19. 9m thick,   and N - value of    this  layer  is   22   /  30
cm.
(b) Causeway Area
This area is composed of sandy silt layer, silty clay layer and silty
sand layer as well. Sandy silt layer in grey colour is 5.7 - 17.0 m thick
and N values are 7 - 2/30 cm. Silty clay layer, partially in grey or brown
colour, has 2.7- 21.6 m thick layer and 20 - 33/30 cm of N values are
observed. Silty sand layer, varies grey, brown to browny grey colour,3.4 -
11.9 m thick and 7 - 50/30 cm of N value are observed at this layer.
(c) Dredging Area
Silt layer and silty sand layer are composed of this area and silt
layer in grey colour, 6.8 m thick, has 6 - 9/30 cm of Nvalue and silty
sand layer, 14.8 m thick, has 12 - 25/ 30 cm of N value.
(2) Weathering Zone
Weathering zone of base rock at the accumulation stratum has been
formed due to  a    long  term operation   of  weathering  and    it  can  be
generally classified as weathered   residuary  soil at   upper   layer    and
weathered rock at lower layer.
Weathered residuary soil at upper layer turns perfectly into
silt and sandy clay by weathering of the base rock and weathered
rock  at  lower   layer  is  very  strong  with elaborateness,   shows    the
structure  and  organization   of  base rock,  contains  schists   partially
even mechanical properties has changed as a base rock though.
-59-



Distribution  at weathering   zone of project    site   shows that
the weathering rock is well developed and weathered residuary soils
covers partially   on  it.     The   thickness  of   weathring   zone   at
receiving terminal area is 0.2m- 10.2 m with 50/1-50/2 of N - value,
3.0 m - 10.5 m thick at causeway area with 50/9 - 50/2 of N - value,
1.8 m thick at dredging area with 50/4 of N - value.
(3) Submarine Topography
Submarine  topography  of   project   site   is  characterized that
accumulated materials   during tidal variation    are   normally composed
of fine mud near Young-      jong   island   and   at  coastal area    and
composed of conchoidal sand and pebbles       where hydrograph    affected
by strong tidal current, however, composed of the mixed combimation
of mud and sand or pebble at some places.
On the other hands, a moderate rock layer has been developed
between Yul   island and Young-jong    island, Jack-yack   island  because
of the strong tidal current flow. Map of submarine topography           is
shown at Fig 5. 1.2.-3.

B. Environmental Impact by Projecte
It  is  expected   that   there   is   no    particular   element  which
brings   significant  changes   in  topography  and   geology    due   to  the
construction   of  the  project,  however,   water  depth   will   be  altered
to (-) 18.6 m artificially at an onshore area by dredging.
Especially,   partial  destruction   of  the   natural   environment   is
anticipated   because  of  the   local  topographical  change    due  to   the
construction   of   receiving  terminal   area  and   causeway,       however,
dredged   soils  from  the  seabed   will   be   substituted     the  required
amount of soil for the construction of receiving terminal area and
causeway.          Total   amount    of   required   soil   and    stone   are

1. Impact Due to Dredging.
Dredging for this project will be carried out to make planed
water  depth  (-) 18.6 m  at  the coastal   area  with    400  m  width   of
channel and  700 m    diameter  of  turning  basin as shown   Fig 5. 1. 2  -
6.     Dredged  earth will   be  totally  utilized   for   the   reclamation
and  construction  of  this  project,     which   can    cover  77.7  %   of
total  required  quantity  of  the project.     Dredging   plans    are   as
follows.
As  shown  in Fig   5. 1. 2 - 7,   turning  basin  of 700  m   diameter
dredged  to  max.  water  depth of   18.6 m, average    water depth  11.0  m
having an 1 : 4 slope from max water depth 14.2 m and min. water
depth  10.9 m  of  the present   and entrance channel   of    400  m   width
will  be  dredged  to water   depth of    18.6 m,    average   water   depth
of  16.1 m  from  the  present  water  depth of 12.0 m   to  20 m.

C. Method for Reducing the Baneful Impact
Required stones for the construction of revetment and causeway
are  planning   to  obtain  from  the   outskirts    of   the  project   site
such  as  400,000 ?d   from  Dong - Chun  Dong,   1,000.000  dn   from  Cho-i
island  and  Hyung-island,   totally 2,400,000 n', since     future   housing
development   project  at Ok-yeon   and  Dong - Chun   Dong  area   will   be
going  at  the   same time   and   excavated   earth   from  Si-hwa   project
would be utilized for Hyung-island.

5.1.3 Marine Ecosystem
A. Present Environmental Condition
1. Investigation Method
a) Sampling
Marine ecosystem has been investigated about chlorophyll,basic produc-
tivity, phyto & zooplankton, egg.larva, floating  animal, benthos,   marine
microorganism etc., at 5 stations by dividing spring & neap tidal period
between Nov. 1990 and May 1991, and refer to existing state of the art.
Qualitative analysis of phytoplankton are carried out as follows.56um
sized Norpac plankton sampler has towed in vertical position and cassified
their species magnifying max. 2,000 times by Olimpus optical microscope (
model BHC ) after fix them to reach 4 % final   concentration   by neutral
formalin.
Clarkebumpus sampler with 5 inch dia. and 160 um sized Nylon-net ( No.
10 ) have been utilized for zooplankton sampling and sampling performance
is done in horizontal position at 1 - 2 m water depth with about   2  knots
speed for 10 minutes.
Investigation about benthos has been carried out at & below tidal land
considering characteristics of area to be investigated. Large scaled
benthos at tidal land are sampled at spring tide and at the place of
inaccessible precepice, a quardrat ( 50 cm X 50 cm ) is installed for
sampling.   And at the area of slime with gentle slope, benthos are sampled
at each 10 m spacing based on Line transect method and strain them through
0.5 dia. mm sieve.   On the other hands, the species not  presented  within
radial area are sampled and investigated qualitatively.   The species which
is difficult to identify has been fixed by 10 % sea     water formalin or
neutral formalin and then identified and accounted at the laboratory and
finally, presented species and no. of individuals are represented as no.s
of individuals per unit meter.
-78-



sO  V  ff  <  >;  D  /                    \X>-d.-; .

(Fig. 5.1.3-1)        Location of Stations for Ecosystem Investigation



b)   Treatment  of  Sample
For quantitative analysis of phytoplankton, sea water is sampled by
Van     dorn sampler and put them into 500 ml poly-ethylene bottle  and  it
has fixed by Lugol solution. The sample has been shielded by aluminium
foil from light in order to prevent photo-oxidation of Indine in Lugol
solution and condensed after   extract water   at upper   layer by   siphon
through more than    48  hrs.  sedim-      entation at    the   laboratory.
Condensed sample is investigated after shaking more than 100 times for
unform distribution of cells. Netplankton has been counted using Olympuss
microscope ( model BHS ) by    extracting 1 ml from sample and putting them
into Sedgwick-Rafter counting chamber and nanoplankton has been accounted
using Palmer-Melony counting chamber. Accounted numbers are converted to
individual no.s   per  unit  volume  ( Cells/ml   ) and Chlorophylla     of
phytoplankton is observed by Turner III Flourometer.    Cold  storaged  sea
water sample in 100 ml poly-ethylene bottle is shaked    well for uniform
Chlorophyl concentration, and then a half of them is used for the
observation of Chlorophyl concentration and the other half is used for the
observation of Chl.a of nanoplankton after filtration of 20 ml sized net.
For correction of Chl. quantity, 500 ml of sea waters are filtrated by
GF/C filter paper on the site and spectrophotometer are utilized for the
observation extracting by 90 % acetone.
The observation of primary productivity is carried out by method of
Parson et al.(  1984  ).   Sampled  sea water   has put   into  the  80  ml
cultivation instrument for productivity observation of   all  plankton  and
sampled sea  water  filtrated   by  20 um   sized net has used     for  the
productivity of nanoplankton.     Furthermore, after C-14 bicarbonate   has
been put into the instrumentation     and above are  cultivated under the
various light condition approximately one and half hours and storaged as
freezed after filtration of 0.45 um   size CF/C   filter  paper.    At  the
laboratory, put acid fuming done filter paper by hydrochloric   acid   into
scintillation cocktail ( Instagel ) and observe DPM value by Liquid
scintillation counter and calculated primary productivity using data of
sunshine amount.
The identification of zooplankton species are performed by Olympus
Zoom     Stereomicroscope ( model SZH ) and Nikon SBR-UK Microscope ( model
SZH ) and Brodskii( 1967 ), Newell( 1977 ), Yamaji( 1979,1983 ), Kim( 1985
) are refered for classification.
-80-



First, large plankton has been chosen from samples for quantitative
ana-     lysis and no.s of all individuals included in samples are counted,
and the rests are subsampled by Stempel pippette and counted at Borogov
tray. Counted numbers are converted to no.s of individuals per unit volume
(inds/ me ) based on filtrated water quantity.
2. Investigation Results
a) Chlorophyl and Basal Productivity
(1) Chlorophyll
Concentration distribution of Chlorophyl at the investigated area
shows     1.02 - 20.10 ug/l and this is lower range of   concentration.  The
reason why lower range of concentration shows is that investigation has
carried out at the season having lower   degree  of  nutrient  salts  as   a
whole.    Above results shows that it is a little higher than 0.13   -  6.20
ug/l of   West sea ( Jang & Shim, 1967 ) and in similar level with   1.91  -
12.67 ug/l of Jeon-soo bay.
Monthly average surface concentration is high in the order of March (
14.5ug/l ), May( 8.00 ug/l ), July( 3.28 ug/l ), October( 2.63 ug/l ) and
concentration at bottom is higher than at surface comparatively. It seems
that distribution inbetween stations is considered uniform, even shows
minor difference as 1.48 - 2.34 ug/l in average though.     Distribution  of
Chlorophyl concentration by Nanoplankton is 0.69 - 2.42 ug/l which occupies
69.4  -  97.4  % of   total  Chlorophyl   concentration  and   do  a   major
contribution on the overall Chlorophyl composition.

Species diversity index shows lower value relatively as 0.91 ( July,
St    3 )- 2.52 ( Oct. St. 3 ), however, it increase in the order    of  May
(1.76 ), Mar. ( 2.02 ), Oct. ( 2.21 ) according to seasonal change.
The reason why the lowest species diversity index present in July is
expected that salinity at inner bay is getting lower due to the effect    of
fresh water and at outer bay, very unstable environment is formed by
presenting minority species frequently, since July is in rainy season.
Also, it is considered that lower species diversity index presented in May
because of higher possessed ratio of S.costatum ( 45 - 82 % ) with    better
optical conditions.

(2) Basal Productivity
Seasonal distribution of basal productivity shows 693.8 mg.C/nd/day
of May, 424.8 mg.C/nt/day of July, 141.5 mg.C/nt/day of October in average
and July & October shows lower basal   productivity.   Such  a  productivity
distribution as above at this area have a trends to be much higher than the
ocean not having active nutrient salts supply by far and less than the area
in  innerbay  polluted  due   to  eutophications.   Reviewing  by  stations,
anabolism ratio at St.3 shows higher value than the other stations and this
is caused by high tranparency, which makes optical transmission in
excellent condition, and high temperature in water.        Anabolism  ratio,
- 84 -



represents primary productivity per unit Chlorophyl, at this area is higher
than circumferencial area as a whole, and this reflects that investigated
area  has  superior   silent  productivity  because  of  excellent   optical
condition  results   higher  productivity  comparatively.    Also,   it    is
considered that most of the basal productivity is generated by Nanoplankton
because basal productivity by Nanoplankton possessed 68.7 - 80.7 %   of   the
total, and thus, above results are coincides well with that the results
from Chlorophyl distribution of Nanoplankton.
Based on the basal productivity survey results at Kyung-ki bay by Jung
& Park( 1,988 ), range of variation( 674 mg.C/ntf/day in Sep. 1,986 & 3,580
mg.C/ " /day in ep. 1,987 ) is higher than this area and 344.2 - 370.4
mg.C/ n /day at Jeon-soo bay in fall based on  the  survey  report  by   Cho(
1,988 ) is less than this investigated area.

b) Zoo & Phytoplankton
(1) Phytoplankton
Analysis results on the data of phytoplankton sampling shows that
Bacillaceae possessed 78 % of total advent species which is 156 speies and
Dinoflagella possessed 15 % and 5 species of Chlorophyceae, 4 species of
Blue-green algae, 2 species of Euglena and Silicoflagella has appeared at
this area. Advent frequency during investigation period are presented in
the order of Paralia sulcata & Nitzschia vitrea in higher rank, and next,
Coscinodiscus radiatus, Cylindrotheca closterium, Ditylum brightwelli,
D.sol, Navicula distans, Skeletonema costatum and Thalassiosira decipiens
etc., and it is considered that these are representative species of
phytoplankton at this area.
Standing crop differs at each station and higher values resulted in
outer sea than in inner sea as a whole.
(a) Species Composition of Phytoplankton
As prescribed above, analysis results on the data of phytoplankton
sampling shows that Bacillaceae possessed 78 % of total advent species
which is 156 species and Dinoflagella possessed 15 % and 5 species of
Chlorophyceae, 4 species of Blue-green algae, 2 species of    Euglena   and
Silicoflagella has appeared at this area. Species appeared diversely in
Bacillaceae  are the   species  belongs  to  genus  Chaetoceros   &   genus
Coscinodiscus and mainly belongs to genus Chaetoceros.    Species  appeared
continuously throughout the year are Skeletonema costatum, Paralia sulcata,
Nitzschia longissima, Cyclotella sp. etc., and the principal species
appeared in summer season are Chaetocera socials, Rhizosolema delicatula,
Cylidrothea closteriium, Gymnodimium sp., Prorocentrum minimum, Euglena sp.
etc., and in fall, Ditylum brightwelli, Eucampia zodiacus, Navicula
salimarum, Euglena sp. etc., has appeared.   In winter,   Paralia  sulcata,
Skeletonema costatum etc., which appears through a year, has appeared.   In
spring,   Chetoecros   nipponicum,   Asterionella   karioma,   Rhizosolenia
delicatula, Thalassiosira condensota, T.rotula etc.,has been appeared
mainly and in this period, a tremendous explosion of Skeletonema costatum
has been resulted in spring especially and except above, Asterionella
karioma, Cylidrothea closteriiium,Nitzschialongissima, Cerataulima dentata,
P.compressump.P.triestinum etc., has appeared and generally outer sea shows
higher value than inner sea.
- 87 -



On the other hands, it is considered that the reduced suspended
ratio caused lower Standing crop of predominant P.sulcata in May & July by
the deterioration of water mixing in vertical due to tide and monsoon
compare to other season, whereas higher Standing crop of predominant
p.sulcata in March & October.

(b)   Standing Crop of Phytoplankton
102,726 Cells/l - 1,217,812 Cells/I of estimated distribution seems
that the range of variation according to station and period is fluctuated.
Standing crop at spring tide is shown a little higher than that at neap
tide,and this is happend by the reason that faster current speed have
Benthos Bacillaceae suspended to surface and at the neap tide, suspension
of Benthos Bacillaceae is not occurred frequently.
Seasonal maximum Standing crop has been resulted in May, and this
is different from a tremendous explosion of Bacillaceae considered as
classical Biomodel of temperate zone coastal area and shows a little late
quantitative increasement periodically.  It is expected that phytoplankton
is increased explosively in May under much more amounts of sunshine, since
- 88 -



the effect of strong current, fresh water influx from north of Gang-hwa

distribution of predominant Skeletonema costatum among phytoplankton is
presented at Fig.5.1.3 - 4.

phenomenon of P.sulcata and S.costatum throughout the year at Jeon-soo  bay
in West sea, however, dominant phenomenon of above species are not observed
at Kyung-ki bay and it has been reported by Choi( 1,984 ) that species in
fresh water & cold water are appeared very frequently, but the variation of
species composition are not observed due to influx of fresh water at this
area and Choi's phytoplankton study results in fall at Kyung-ki bay ( 1,982
) shows that C.debilis, E.zodiacus, S.costatum are appeared as dominant
species at overall bay areas.

(2) Zooplankton
According to seasonal appearance phase of zooplankton, average
amount of appearance revealed 1,763 Inds/nt in March and 9,950 Inds/ vi of
max. amount of appearance has      investigated  in October.      Appeared
zooplankton has been identified as 4 classified group and Copepods occupied
the most of appeared zooplankton.
(a) Species Composition of Zooplankton
Zooplankton in this area comprises Protozoa, Cladocerans, Copepods,
Chaetognaths, Appendicularia, Mysid, Euphausiid, Plaktonic polychaete, and
11 paedo group species and 2 fresh water species ( Ploima, Branchiopoda
).Many research report ( Parsons et al.,1981: Raymont,1980 ) has been
investigated that Copepods    are predominant  in   the   aggregation   of
zooplankton. Shim & Park( 1982 ), Shim & Noh( 1982 ), Shim & Lee( 1983 ),
Shim & Yoon( 1987 ) etc., repeatedly  reported  same research results   as
above at coastal area of Korea.  It is revealed that dominant  species of
zooplankton are P.crassirostris, A.clausi, Copepds larva in March and
N.scintillans,  Copepods  larva,  A.clausi  in May  and   P.crassirostris,
Cirripedia larva, C.affinis, P.parvus in October.
(b) Standing Crop of Zooplankton
Standing crop distribution of zooplankton is 1,106 - 26,033
Inds/nd and range of variation according to station & period is diverse.
Generally, Standing crop of March is less than that of July and this
occurred by the reason that phytoplankton reduction due to the engorgement
of zooplakton which turns to food shortage of zooplankton and mass
breedings of paedo-Zoea reversely, and thus, Standing crop of zooplankton
is becoming more reduced.
Monthly average no.s of individuals are 1,763 Inds/nt in March,
13,658 Inds/7d in May, 9,367 Inds/it in July, 9,950 Inds/nt in October and
minimum in March and maximum  in May are exist respectively.        Taking
consideration of the alteration of seasonal average no.s of individuals,
1,834, 9,364, 9,658, 12,050 Inds/ni has revealed in March, May, July,
October respectively and it tends to decrease rapidly since gradual
increase between March and October. In other words, no.s of zooplankton
individuals at this area shows the change of concentration according to
- 92 -



tidal & seasonal variation, and maximum concentration is observed at neap
tides in fall and at spring tide in spring, intermediate concentration is
at spring tide in summer & fall and at neap tide in winter, least
concentration is observed at spring tide in winter.
At neap tide in summer, Copepds such as Copepodite, Nauplius,
Paracalanus  parvus,  P.crassirotris,   A.clausi,   A.pacifica,   C.affinis,
Oithona sp. etc., are dominant at overall sea area, and Decapoda larva,
Biralve larva also appeared at overall sea area, and a great no.s of
Decapoda larva has appeared. Standing crop is similar in all cases without
apparent tendency, however, it tends to a little higher at inner bay area.
Considering by stations, higher Standing crop is revealed in the order of
St.4,5,3,2,1 and tends towards outer sea as a whole.
(C) Distribution of Dominant Species
Dominant species occupies 10 % of total amounts of appearance are
Paracalanus parvus, Acartia bifilosa, A.clausi, Corycaeus affinia etc., of
Copepods and Zoea, Copepodite etc., of larva group and predominant species
among them are A.bifilosa, A.claudi, Zoea.     Especially, A.bifilosa  shows
high appearance frequency at period of spring tide and diminish rapidly   at
period of neap tide, and Zoea larva does same as well, and it is considered
that such diminution is related to the environmental change ( water
temperature, salinity, alteration of natural enemy ) of A.bifilosa and Zoea
larva.     At  neap  tide   in summer,  Copepodite,  Nauplius,  Paracalanus
parvus, P.crassirotris, A.clausi, A.pacifca, C.affinis, Oithona   sp.  etc.,
of Copepods are dominant at overall sea area, Decapoda larva and Biralve
larva appears at the overall sea area either and a great many no.s of
individuals  has presented.       At  spring  tide,Copepodite,  C.nauplius,
P.parvus, P.crassirotris, A.clausi, A.pacifica etc., of Copepods are
dominant.        At neap tide in fall, N.scintillans   is dominant   at  the
overall sea area and at the inner bay area, and at the outer bay area,
higher possessed ratio revealed and   P.parvus,  P.crassirostris,  A.clausi,
A.pacifica, Oithona sp., Copepodite appeared.

(3) Mutual relations between Zooplankton and Phytoplankton
In general, increment of zooplankton follows right after increment
of phytoplankton and it does not exhibit mutual relations with the quantity
of phytoplankton in fall season.        Above may be occurred by   the  reason
that predominant N.scintillans in this season is in full flourish induced
by environmental factor such as stability of water    etc.      On  the  other
hands, the increasement of Netphytoplankton brings the increasement of
Zooplankton   and   reversely,   decreasement    of   Netphtoplakton    brings
decreasement of Zooplankton with a time lag.

C) Egg.Larva and Nekton
(1) Egg.Larva
It is revealed that fishegg appears from May through September and
mostly appeared at inner bay in May and Ilisha elongata egg is decreasing
and Engraulis japonica egg is increasing in June to compare with May.   In
July, Ilisha elongata egg and Engraulis japonica egg appeared a little,
however, the quantity is considerably reduced amount to compare with that
in May & June.   By taking consideration of appearances period of  fry,  it
is regarded that egg laying season at the investigated area is, for the
most part, December thru February and April thru June, and as a fish laying
egg in cold water season, there are Pholis taczanowskii in between January
& February, Lateolabrax japonicus and Hemiramphus villosus in February,
Hexagrammos otaki  and H.sajori   in around December.        Also,   it  is
regarded that Fugu niphobles, Fugu sp. & Arelisous phomaleus are laying
eggs in July thru August, Pleunonichthys cornutus in October, and all
others considered laying eggs in between April and June.
(a) Eggs
- Species Composition
At the outer bay of investigated area, Engraulis japonica,
Cynoglossinae gen.sp and Callianymus gen.sp appears and Konosirus japonica
in Kyung-ki bay and Herklostichthys zunasi in outer sea area appears
frequently.      2 - 3 species has appeared at each station in spring tidal
period and a vivid eggs-laying of H.zunasi & C.gen.sp are shown and
especially, appearance of C.gen.sp is frequent.
-   Appearance Quantity
Appearance quantity of fisheggs varies from 1,219 Inds/n to
3,696 Inds/nd and Callionnymus gen.sp, Cynolossinae gen.sp, which shows
frequent appearance, occupies 76 % & 16 % respectively and thus, these are
regarded as predominant species in this    area.       Also,  Callionnymus
appeared  at both spring    and neap tide and appearance quantity       of
Herklotsichthys zunasi at spring tide is much more than that at neap tide.
As a result, 9,071 Inds/1,000 m of total 5 species at spring tide appeared
and took 59 % of total appearance quantity and at neap tide, 6,184 Inds/nt
of total 6 species appeared and took 41 % of total appearance quantity.
- 97 -



(b) Larvae
- Species Composition
Larva has been investigated as 13 genus and 15 species totally,
and diverse range of variation is shown as min. 3 species to max. 11
species and stations near coastal area( St. 1 & 2 ) reveals less frequency
of appearance than the stations at outer sea area ( St. 3,4, & 5 ).
-   Appearance Quantity
Appearance quantity of larva has investigated as 3,349 Inds/1,000
m and at spring tide, appears 3,233 Inds/1,000 t ,thus, took 97 % of total
no.s of individuals, and at neap tide, appears 116 Inds/1,000 Vt.
H.zunasi which shows the most appearance quantity appears 2,658 Inds/1,000
m3 and occupies 82 % of total no.s of individuals, therefore, it is
considered as a principal fish.
(c) Nekton
Total 46 species of fish has been observed at this area and appears
28 species in 3 class gill net, 27 species in a dragnet and 24 species in a
temporarynet and seasonally in April, the most appearance of 22 species and
the least appearance of 5 species in December are revealed.      Gobiidaee
sp. & Flounder as a fixing benthonic fish at near shore area has appeared
throughout the year among the investigated fishes and the others shows
change of appearance aspect according to seasonal change.      And  it  is
investigated  that Gobiidae, Engraulis   japonica,  Konosirus   qunctatus,
Callionmus sp. are the principal fishes in summer season and principal fish
in winter season is Enedrias sp..
On the other hands, monthly appropriate demand of fishery and
migration route map of certain dominant fishes at the west sea includes
investigated area are shown in Appendix 12.1 thru 18.
(d) Benthos
The investigated area, where have a excessive tidal range, reveals
layer distribution of dominant organism group and shows wider distribution
of vertical layer relatively to compare with other   sea area.      During
investigation period, maximum no.s of species appeared is in summer season(
July ) and minimum no.s of species appeared is in winter season(January),
- 98 -



and it tends to increase greatly from March to July and to decease
gradually from October to January. Predominant animal group is Polychaeta
and possessed 86.4 %in Feb, 72.0 % in May, 73.6 % in Jul, 93.4 % in Oct. of
total appearance.     Appearance by stations, St. a is the highest and St.
e is the  lowest.     Habitation   density  of  other  animal  group  except
Polycheta is much poor, and it is specially noteworthy that Amphipoda and
Asteroidea are considerably important animal group in other coastal area or
bay, whereas appearance of these is very much poor.
-   Organisms  at Tidal   Land
Chthamalus challengeri at upper layer( St.c ) and Crassostrea
gigas at lower layer ( St.e ) of tidal land are built up predominant
species  group  for  an  adhesive  organism   and Gloiopeltis    furcata   &
Myelophycus simplex at upper layer, Ulva pertusa & Sargassum thunbergi &
Corallina piluifera at the layer down to middle lower part and Undaria
pinnatifida at the lowest layer are dominant for a marine algae.
Distribution of individual no.s per unit area has been revealed
that Chthamalus challengeri, which is one of adhesive organism, is found as
a predominant species closing in upon 400 Inds/100 mt at the upper layer
of tidal land( St.c ),   and  at  lower  layer(  St.e  ),  Lasaea  undulata,
Crassostrea gigas, Lattorina brevicila, Patelloida pygmaea, kinds of small
shellfish, are dominant   in  sequence.         As  a  whole,  3  groups  of
organism such as Crustacea of Arthropoda, Mollusca and Polychaeta of
Annelida are consist of major portion of organisms, but Echinodermata,
Insecta & Pycnogonida are also shown somehow.
Diversity of dominant species group has not been found at this
investigation comparing to other areas in West & South sea, and it is
expected that environmental change due to settling of suspended material
have already been affected to physiognomy alteration of benthos by the
reason of accumulation of reducing mud inbetween individuals which forms
Oyster  gathering.       On   the other   hands,  Mollusca,   Crustacea   of
Arthropoda, Polychaeta of Annelida, Echinodermata, Cnidaria with fixation
and Bryozoa, Brachiopoda, pycnogonida, Tunicata of Protochordata appeared
as a biota at the below tidal land. Diogenes edwardsii has been revealed
as predominant species by occupying 40 % of total no.s of appeared
individuals ( appearance of 586 individuals ), and Amphioplus megapomus is
taken 17 % of total.

- Marine Algae
A biota of marine algae comprises 19 species totally which
consists of 1 specy of Blue-green algae, 8 species of Chlorophyceae, 3
species of Brown algae, 7 species of Red algae and it has been reported by
Lee( 1981 ) that 103 species distributed over  this  area.    By  seasonal
frequency of appearance, 16 species, which is the most,  has appeared   in
spring and 8 species, which is the least, has appeared in summer.  A biota
of marine algae is very poor at this investigation area by the reason that
unfavorable environmental conditions for growth of marine algae are derived
from the much turbid seawater owing to the reclamation project of
circumferencial area   and the poor exposed rocks of       islands  except
Keun-ga-ri, Jack-eun-ga-ri, Pal-mi islands.
(e) Marine Microorgannism
A range of individual no.s of microorganism at this area has
revealed in the range of 1 X 103 - 3 X 103  Cells/ml  as  a whole  and  in
detail, 1 X 103 - 1 X 105 Cells/ml in March, 3 X 104 - 5 X 105 Cells/ml  in
May, 1 X 105 - 3 X 106 Cells/ml in July, 4 X io4 - 2.2 X  lo5  Cells/ml  in
October.      The ranges shown above  is determined a    little higher  at
spring tide than neap tide and at stations near coastal area ( St. 1,2,3 ),
and it is regarded that above have happened due to the inflow of organism
such as sewage etc, from the near land, Nam-koo and Nam-dong koo of Incheon
city, Shi-heung city, however their differences are slight.
Also, the range of appearance shows apparent seasonal change in the
de creasing order of summer, autumn, spring and winter, and it is denoted
that water temperature is the major element which can affect the living
condition of germs.   By water depth, it  is  increased  in the order   of
bottom, middle, surface and there is a slight difference according to
season and stations in it.
On the other hands, based on the results of DAPI direct counting and
numerical counting by cultivation, investigated area belongs to the middle
of Oligotrophic and Mesotrphic from the Eutrophication point of view, and
comparatively high no.s of cultivated individuals of Colitis germs,
Salonella-shigeela and Vibrio to other area denotes investigated area
polluted somewhat.

B.   Environmental  Impacts by Project
Impacts on marine ecosystem caused by dredging and stone pouring for
reclamation project can be described as short term & long term impacts and
direct & indirect impacts based upon their characteristics. Expected short
term & direct impacts due to reclamation and dredging construction works
may be physical destruction & removal of habitat on the progress of
construction works, primary productivity reduction due to SS, suffocation
of  fish.shellfish,  reduction of food,    escape   of   nekton,   paratism
disturbance, toxic damage by suspension & eruption of toxicant, creation of
a mutation, physiological weakening etc.
Long term & indirect impacts expected to be occurred are species
composition change of organism because of erosion location change, change
of congregation distribution, interception and/or destroy of food chain,
change  of fish reccurence route,     change of    metabolism   activation,
distribution, species composition of organism caused by stratification of
water temperature and dissolved oxygen due to increased water depth, and
flow exchange & current velocity reduction which can produce salinity
change, red tide, alteration of sea water quality according to inflow
amount of pollutants and sewage and current velocity increasement which can
produce change of fish recurrence route, reduction of primary productivity,
water level fluctuation and paratism disturbance etc.
Alteration of marine and physical environment due to reclamation and
dredging works for LNG receiving terminal project can be created by the
change of coastline and the most important element which can affect marine
ecosystem near project site is turbidity alteration by the increasement of
SS and this kind of change is based on the earth & stone pouring and
dredging of sea lane and earth disposal occurred in the process of
reclamation.
Thus, area having plenty of biota gets no impacts due to the
construction of causeway section "A", since most of the above area are
exist within Song island reclamation area ( "A" section of causeway of this
project - 3,884m X 8m is included ), however, impacts created by the
construction of causeway "B" and SS concentrat on increasement, extinction
of tidal land due to reclamation for LNG project are as follows.
-104 -



1. Impacts due to SS Increasement by Earth Disposal
As SS dipersed in water, physical change such as change of turbidity &
colour, SS increasement, reduction of radiation intensity are expected to
be occurred and burying of Benthos is anticipated to be followed due to
above physical change like settlement of earL-h.
2. Impacts due to Eruption, Secession, Dispersion of Toxicants
From the raised impacts by SS, physical impacts are occupies most of
impacts to be occured and affects Fish, Shellfish, marine algae due to SS,
whereas chemical impacts according to the eruption of nutrient salts are
not serious.
Therefore, it is anticipated that Acantia clausi, Oithoni nana,
Chaetoceros spp etc., which is strong enough to resist polluted water, will
be increased but weaker planktons against polluted water will be decreased.
Take shellfish for an example, Tapes philippinarum shows a sudden jump
of excretion under the condition of mud suspension concentration over 500
ppm and oxygen consumption has been decreased sharply under the condition
of over 5 ppm for Oyster and Turbo cornutus and over 10 ppm for Tapes
philippinarum, and over 16 ppm for Oyster and over 300 ppm for Tapes
philippinarum, amount of water filtration is decreased  as well.     Among
bivalves, Oyster, Mitilus crassitesta and Tapes philippinarum can survive
at the sand layer more than the sandy mud layer.    Comparing lethal effect
of sedimented mud on bivalves by LD ( Median Lethal Day ), it has been
resulted that Oyster can survive 11 days at sand layer and 9 days at sandy
mud layer, Mitilus crassitesta can survive 9 days at sand layer and 7- 8
days at sandy mud, Tapes philippinarum survive 12 days and 9 days
respectively.
Major impacts due to mud suspension on Marine algae can be classified
as reduction of solar light, sedimentation and/or adhesion of suspended mud
and  physical  damages.     Mud suspension   may  bring  deterioration  of
germination ratio and of survival ratio, delay of growth and disturbance of
photosynthesis.   If depth of mud sedimentation becomes more than  0.3  mm,
then ratio of germination and survival of Porphyra tenera Kiellman would be
decreased. Under the condition of 25 - 75 ppm, sprout of seaweed would be
fallen off, hence, secondary sprout will not be produced.
-105-



Taking the case of Undaria pinnatifida, survival ratio of sporophyte
will be decreased under the condition of over 100 ppm of suspended mud
concentration and 0.05 - 0.02 mm sedimentation of suspended mud enforce
growth of sprouts to delayed, and the growth of seaweed may be delayed
under the condition of mud suspension concentration over 10 ppm.   Over 150
ppm, degree of optical absorption would be reduced and over 200 ppm, photo
synthesis is hindered.   For Undaria pinnatifida,  mud  suspension produce
the reduction of optical light in seawater and furthermore, intercept
yellow light with 570 - 750 nm and red light with 630 - 660 nm which are
necessarily effective for photosynthesis.    Form the above annalysis,it is
noted that a severe impact on marine organisms could be happened in 30 - 50
ppm.
3. Impacts due to Extinction of Tidal Land
It is expected that an alteration of natural environment will be
followed, as physical change is taken by the reclamation process of tidal
land.    By observing impacts on ecosystem of tidal land during reclamation
process, impacts may be classified as about plankton, surface of adhesive
or  creeping  earth,  underground  animal  and fish,   and   reduction   of
gastropods( Hinia festiva, Batillaria mulfiformis, Umbonium costatum ) and
crabbs( Philyra pisum, Macrophthalmus japonicus, Macrophthalmus dilatatus )
is anticipated as surface animal and Meretrix lusoria, Mactra veneriformis,
Cyclina sinensis in Lamelli branchia and Nereis japonica in Polychaeta and
Natica severa in Gastropoda is anticipated to be reduced.
In case of Japan, the amount of fishery catch per unit common water
reclamation area 1 d   is reported to be reduced as much as 6ton, and thus,
4.8 ton of fishery catch amount reduction is expected by applying above
design criteria and however, considerable reduction of fishery catch amount
is anticipated.
4. Phytoplankton
Increasement of suspended solids produced by dregding and earth
pouring during the process of construction may disturb photosynthesis of
phytoplankton and induce the temporary reduction on spacial distribution
and productivity. Chaetocevos socialis and Skeletonema   costatum,  appears
very frequently regardless season, will moves  to outer   sea  and  Acantia
clausi, Chaetoaeros sp., Oithona nana which resist strongly to polluted
water will be increased and vise versa.
-106-



Impacts derived from the change of coast line after completion which
can affect on marine ecosystem are as follows.   As prescribed in  previous
chapter, it is anticipated that current speeds are going to be increased 5
cm/sec, 2cm/sec, 1 cm/sec during flood tide at SC -1, SC - 9, SC - 11 and
12 cm/sec, 1 cm/sec, 17 cm/sec, 1 cm/sec, 4 cm/sec at SC - 1, SC - 10, SC -
11, SC - 12, C - 1 during ebb tide respectively and therefore, above
increased current speed will result heavier turbidity and reduction of
primary productivity by disturbing a lump of water.
However after completion of this project, it is considered that
primary productivity reduction area will be decreased preferably because
average current speeds at flood tide are 83 cm/sec, 78 cm/see, which are 4
cm/see, 6 cm/see less than original state and at the rest area, current
speeds are expected to decrease 6.6 cm/sec from average flood tide and 16.3
cm/sec from average ebb tide, and therefore, above induce stagnation of
water lump and deterioration of water quality taking impacts on general
marine ecosystem, but impacts are limited to a certain area, thus, it is
considered to be negligible.
On the other hands, basd on the facts that standing crop of
Phytoplankton appears higher at neap tide having a stable water lump than
at spring tide, and inducing of great appearance of plankton after great
stock of nutrient salts, appearance of Prorocentrum tristinum etc., which
would be a red tide source organism at St.2 - St.5 under the survey of
standing crop, there are possibilities that red tide may be occurred at the
area  having  reduced  current  speed  and stratification of crowd      and
anticipation on the alteration of primary productivity around entry sealane
and turning area and species composition change of plankton due to
disturbance of water lump.
5. Zooplankton
It is considered that great appearance of Noctiluce scintillans would
not be happened, since water level after project completion can be changed
like 1 cm increase/decrease at PT - 1 during high & low water level and at
T - 1, 2 cm decrease in high water level and 1 cm increase in low water
level and at T - 2, 4 cm decrease in H.W.L and 1 cm increase in L.W.L etc.,
hence, differences are negligible.
However, following alterations may be expected according to SS
concentration change. At the northeast tidal land to be used as causeway,
larvae of Zooplankton, Mactra veneriformis, Cyclina sinensis, Meretrix
-107 -



lusoria, Solen gouldi, Tapes philippinarum and other larvae of shellfish
have been sampled and especially St.5 is a very important habitat for
larvae, therefore, SS concentration increasement due to this project will
cause the reduction of harvest and larvae sensitive to environmental change
decreased, thus, induce change of Benthos and there is a feasibility to
affect the   growth and feeding of eggs of       invertebrate  animal   by
sedimentation of SS on sea bottom.
6. Marine Algae
Reduction of primary productivity and standing crop are expected to be
decreased in the case that impacts are given to the environment judging
from anticipated increasement of SS concentration and presummed value of
inorganic nutrient   salts  in water  to be followed.       In   addition,
considering primary productivity observed at each station by effect of
light intensity due to SS, simulated SS increasement after  completion of
the project has been revealed that it would move to the coast of in-land at
flood tide and move to the outer sea with dispersion at ebb tide and
comprehensive increasement of SS concentration at high water level is
distributed and dipersed over northwest to southeast direction along the
coast line from centerline of causeway, and curve of 1 ppm concentration
increasement have showed to nearside of Incheon harbour in northwest
direction and to front area of Ansan city in southeast direction with max.
width of 10 km and max. length of 30 km, and in conclusion, concentration
increasement and dispersion range of SS are extensive comparatively.
Above is caused by the reason of wide tidal land at this area and shallow
water depth at high tide and especially, SS concentration is not increased
rapidly at dredged channel area because of faster current speed and deep
water depth regardless of silt protector installation, however, impact
transfered an important effect to tidal land of the coast.     Namely,  SS
produced due to dredging of channel moves with dispersion towards to Ansan
city via southern part of LNG receiving terminal by current and affected
area of   SS concentration   increasement  without  installation of   silt
protector become wider than with installation of silt protector.        In
other words, areas increasedover 10 ppm are 37.2 XA in case 1, 35.9 A in
case 2, 32.0 dAA in case 3 and thus, 14 % has been decreased and    it  is
predicted that SS is dispersed radially from the northern spillway location
of LNG receiving terminal at low tide.   And pollutant  numerical  modeling
analysis have resulted that areas increased over 10 ppm are 29.5    d,  in
case 1, 28.2 dA  in case 2 which denote 4 % reduction, 26.2 kd  in case  3
which are reduced 11 %.
-108-



From the above results, primary productivity and standing crop of
Phytoplankton will be decreased somewhat and decrease of species no.s and
standing crop of Zooplankton are expected accordingly.
On the other hands, it has been reported that feasibility is exist to
do young fishes and large Benthos harm when SS concentration increases over
50 ppm, however, areas increased over 30 ppm for this project are limited
to 1.5 ka at high tide and 1.7 kg at low tide in case 1, 1.4 da# at high
tide and at low tide in case 3 and areas having over 50 ppm increase are
expected to be restricted to a certain localized area.
And photosynthesis quantity of Marine algae is evaluated to be
decreased 7 - 24 % annually at the area increased over 10 ppm and
therefore, germination ratio and survival ratio of marine algae, delay of
growth and interference on photosynthesis are expected to be occurred and
thus, decrease of egg.larva, nekton and Benthos in no.s of species and
quantity will be produced momentarily according to standing crop decrease
of phytoplankton due to above.
Also, target distribution of organism would be changed as waterdepth
changes and moreover, current speed change can cause the alteration of
scouring and sedimentation of seabottom and then, comprehensive change of
ecosystem such as distribution and species of organism may be occurred.
However, it has been predicted that impacts on eggs.larvae and Benthos due
to this project is momentarily and restricted to a localized area, since
change of tide level and current speed are slight and negligible.
7. Benthos
Recently, shallow water area of Korea is polluted by the preparation
of industrial site and tidal land development project which cause change of
water environment and a great many suspension muds and hence, damage of
cultivated organisms in shallow water becomes a matter of grave concern and
suspended materials in the seawater is the direct reason of death from
suffocation of fish and Shellfish by reducing light intensity in seawater
and interfering photosynthesis.
(a) Shellfish
Generally, shellfish is a wide salt nature specy that inhabit in
the sandymud and within the range of 11 - 28 'C  water  temperature  and  a
tremendous impact is given to shellfishes at the West sea where large
-109-



scaled development project such as harbour construction etc., is in
progress.     In this project, suspended muds are produced due to  dredging
and it is found that particles with large grain size are going to
sedimented at the near area but particles with fine grain size( silt or
clay ) are suspended and dispersed extensively.     It  is known well    by
Hyang-cheon-soo-shi( 1974 ) and Aei-wan-soo-shi( 1974,1975 ) that closing
and opening of shellfish and water filtration ratio would be deteriorated
if seawater includes  plenty of   suspended mud.       Also,  it has   been
reported that suspended mud in the seawater becomes over 6.5 ppm, then
impact may be given to the closing and opening of Bozoo shellfish and 10 %
of Tapes philippinarum will be dead in the case that sedimented materials
of the width of a shell covers on it( Chon-sang, 1975 ) and Nordotis discus
will be dead completely within a very short time.
Moreover, a report has been presented that scoured earth and mud
from revetment covers on the overall cultivation farm with a depth of 1 - 3
cm then serious damage can impact to the organisms inhabitant in tidal land
after completion of the project if shellfish cultivation farm is located
close to harbour facilities or revetment.
Based on the survey result on Meretrix lusoria due to impact of
suspended mud by Jang( 1976,1978 ), it has been revealed that through 30
days passing, death of larval shellfish has been shown first and in the
order of medium and grown up shellfish and more than 50 % of Meretrix
lusoria has been dead between 39 and 43 days during 46 days of cultivation
covering 10 cm depth of mud on 2.5 - 5.5 cm shell length of Meretrix
lusoria.    From the above, the reason why death of larval Meretrix lusoria
happens first is considered that larva takes more severe interferance from
the  inappropriate  environment  than   grown-up,   whereas   physiological
metabolism of larva is more active than that of grown-up.    On  the other
hands, on the test by suspended concentration, 3.5 - 4.5 cm shell length of
Meretrix lusoria has not been dead for 65 day under 100 ppm but 10 %of
death has been shown inbetween 49 - 55 days if concentration reaches to 500
ppm and 50 % of death under 1,000 ppm inbetween 50 - 51 days.
On the suspended mud impact test on metabolism of gills, oxygen
consumption of gills has not been reduced greatly until concentration of
suspended mud reaches to 1,000 ppm.     Based on the above results, it has
been  predicted   that  shellfishes at   this  area are keeping    stronger
capability to resist than other area even differences of reaction are exist
according to concentration and settling time of suspended mud though, and
death of shellfish will definitely occurred if higher concentration
continues for a long time.
-110-



C. Methods for Reducing the Baneful Impact
First of all, it is very important to predict the impacts to be
occurred by the interception of pollutants and periodical observation,
since it is very hard to predict impacts of ecosystem by pollutants
produced from the construction of the project.     Therefore, dispersion of
pollutants shall be protected by the installation of silt protector during
reclamation works and it is required to establish proper woking time
schedule to reduce emmision of pollutants by periodical observation of SS
concentration and turbidity around reclamation area.
Also, to prevent impacts on marine ecosystem by pollutants produced
from the LNG receiving terminal facilities while operation and to preserve
durable  marine ecosystem,   experimental   cultivation   farm   shall   be
constructed and perform more than 2 times of annual marine ecosystem
observation for the purpose of post management on environment.



5. 1. 4 Marine Environment
A. Present Environment Condition
The  project site is situated   at  the   inside Kyoung-ki Bay    which
is  surrounded   by   various   magnitude   islands   such   as  Young-jong
island,  Young-you   island,   Moo-uei   island,  Pal-mi  island   etc    at
northwest  sea  and Dae - boo    island,  Young -hueng island,   Kye  -  wol
island  etc  at  southwest  sea,  therefore  it does    not   affected    by
direct  wave   impact   on   site   area.  Moreover,    entry   of   Incheon
harbour  is  a  long,  narrow sea   lane,  whereas   there   are   big   and
wide  tidal  land  at both side of   sea   lane.
Water  depth of   this  area   is  about   2  m    refering   to  Chart
Datum  and  20 m - 30 m  & over by    approaching  to  central area  of  the
bay.   Tidal  current  flows  along  the main   hydrographic way south    to
north  and  the velocity   of  current   is 3 - 4 knots   at  spring   tide,
1.3 m/sec  at  flood  tide  2.0 m/sec  at  ebb  tide.
1. Tide
Observed  period of   tide  at  the wharf   of Dae - boo island    near
project  site  shows  that  there   are  almost   similar  high   tide   and
low  tide  every  month  with wide   difference  at ebb   tide  and   little
difference  at  flood   tide    in   imquality   of  tidal   time,   whereas
opposite  phenomenon   in  inequality  of  high tide  level.  Also,  it   is
observed  that  higher  level  of  high   tide follows   right   after   low
level of low tide at this area and average high tide interval is
7 min.  faster (around  4hrs  21 min after  the    meridian   transit)  than
that of Incheon.
Tidal  ranges  at  Dae - boo    island   are   800.2  cm   for  spring,
500.1 cm for mean, 329.9 cm for neap, these are a little bit more
or  less  than  that  of   Incheon,  797.8 cm  for spring,   572.4  cm   for
mean,  347.0 cm  for  neap  and  approx. H.H.W and   H. W.  0.  S.  T.   are
926.4 cm and 863.3 cm respectively.
