2. Tidal Current Flow
Tidal  current  flow  at this   site area   is   formed   an  alliance
of  the  current  flow  to the west,    Pal-mi  island, in high  tide   and
of  the  current  flow of   Dong-su Do   and Seo -sudo    etc,   and   then
turns the direction to the north abruptly.
Above  tidal  current  flow tends    to   dig   the   shore   line of
Incheon,  Song  island,  A - am  island  and   especially   at   ebb  tide,
tends to dig the shoreline of Young - jong island under the effect
of  sunken  rocks  at  the central   area of hydrograph.   Likewise,   main
hydrograph  at  flooding  tide create   and  expand  the  tidal   land   at
the project site and the western area.
In the   mean while,   the velocity of    tidal  current   is   5.1  -
11.0 cm/sec  in the direction of     flooding  tidal   current,   and   the
distribution of   current varies   to decreasing    non  -  linearly   from
surfuce of water to the seabed.
-115-

3. Wave
Surrounding  islands  and  tidal   lands  around   project   site   and
Incheon   harbour   can   prevent   the    site   from    buiding    up    a
significant  wave. Generally,  the   reason of   wave   formation   can   be
described  as  one  of  the    two   elements   according   to   the   local
exposure  condition,  one   is  due  to  the  northwest   wind   in   winter
season,  the  other   is  due  to  the   typhoon   oriented   scuthwest   in
summer  season.    Wave  heights   for   Incheon   harbour   are   excerpted
from " Estimation  report  of   design  wave  for  marine  facility      and
described here with at table 5. 1. 4 - 2.
( Table5.1.4-2)            Wave data for Incheon

examined  by  the  wind   data  for  past  15 years,   the   calm  condition
of  sea  under  0.5 m  or   less  of  significant  wave  height   has   been
occupied  about   93 % of   the  total,  6.6  %  under  0.5  -  0.99  m   of
significant  wave  height,   0.5 %  under   1.0  -  1.49m   of   significant
wave  height,  0.01 %   under  1.5 - 1.99 m  of  significant   wave   height
and  occurrence  of  significant  wave over 2m   has  investigated  as   one
time  in a year,   big and   severe  waves  are  produced  by monsoon    and
concentrated  in winter   season . ( Table  5. 1. 4 - 3 ).

4. Litoral Drift
a) Suspended Solid
Observed   quantity   of   suspended   solid   are    64  -   175  mg/l   at
spring   tide   and  19 - 62 mg/l   at   neap  tide,   which    means   that   the
concentration     of  suspended   solid   at  spring   tide   is  3 times   higher
than   that  at   neap  tide. This    happens  mainly    due    to   transportion
of   the  wave and   current,   since   the  site   area  has    a   wide    tidal
land which is silt layer with a fine particle.

b) Tractive drift
Survey   result   shows    that    the   distributions     of  tractive    at
project   site   drift   are  372 - 440 g    at  flood   tide   and 310-421 g    at
ebb   tide  for   a  half    period    of    spring    tide,  therefore     it    is
regarded   that   the   movement   of  tractive   drift is    governed     by   the
tidal current velocity.

b) Consolidation Ratio
Consolidation  ratio  which   is  the  index  of    bottom  sediments
stability has analyzed as follows at this project site.
Lapsed  time  distribution for  consolidation    ratio   of  0.5,   the
depth of sediment layer at any time becomes one -half of sediment
layer,  is  about  average  0.4 hrs ( 0.11 - 0.55hrs ) at St. M - 1      and
0.42 hrs ( 0.11 - 0.46 hrs ) at St. M-2     as  shown  in  table  5. 1. 4  -
14  and  15. Therefore,  sediments  at  St. M - 2    are  stabilized  faster
than  at  St. M - 1,   in other   words,  re-suspension   may  be   occurred
more frequently at St. M - 1 than at St. M - 2.

B. Environmental Impact by Project
Numerical   modeling  analysis   has  been  performed    to  survey    the
primary   factor  on  the   basis  of  item  by   item about the    impact   on
marine environment due to the construction of Incheon LNG receiving
terminal   area,  with  the   modeling ( K -  cythere   )   of  tides,    tidal
velocity,   discharge  of   tides  and  the  modeling (cytengel    )   of   the
movement of suspended solid.
1. Current Flow Modeling ( K - cythere )
a) Description of Modeling
K - cythere   modeling  system   is  the  newly    developed  numerical
analysis   modeling  system   for  tidal  current   by   the  association    of
power   and  electric  co, ( LNH ) and     SOGREAH    Co,  in   France.    This
program   can  estimate   tidal  level  and    velocity  due  to    the   tidal
movement under finite grid system by solving two (2) - dimensional
Saint - Venant   equation   and  the basic  assumption for    above    are   as
follows.
- Currenty velocity is the mean value of water depth.
- Vertical    acceleration    which   means   variation    due   to    the
disparity of water pressure is negligible.
Basic equation under above assumptions is as below.
az     au     av
-+             - = 0
at     ax     ay
-quations of Motion

Where,  (I Term for Momentum Variation According to Time
@ Term for Advection
® Term for Propagation
( Term for friction of water surface
® Term for friction of Sea Bottom
® Term for Torbulent Diffusion of Horizontal Momentum
T Term for tranfering force
x, y         Coordinate
t          :Time
z(x, y, t)    Height  from Reference   surface  to  Free  Water
Surface
h(x, y, t)   Water Depth from Free Surface to Sea Bottom
FIF(x, y)    Distance from Reference   Surface  to  Sea  Bottom
(Positive)
When Sea Bottom is Above Reference Surface,
Negative in Reverse)
U(x, y, t), V(x, y, t) : Discharge Per unit Width in x, y
Direction
u(x, y, t), v(x, y, t) : Current velocity in x, y Direction
g          : Gravity Acceleration
f          : Coriolis coefficient
sx,   sy : Water Surface Shear Stress Due to  wind   in x,  y
Direction
bx,   by : Bottom Shear Stress due to Flow in x, y Direction
, bx     p g    U  IU/C2 h2,  by = p g V IuI/C2 h2
C            Chezy friction coefficient
Sea Water Density
K             Turbulent  Diffusion  Coefficient  of  Horizontal
Momentum
Description of above variables are presented at Fig 5.1. 4 -
13,  and  Qx ( i , j ) and Qy ( i , j ) are      as  below.
Qx ( i , j ):  Discharge  at  mid point   hetween   grid point(i,j) and
(i+l, j)
Qy ( i , j ):  Discharge  at  mid  point  between     grid   point(i,j)
and (i, j+l)
Now,  discharge  and  sea water  level   of   each   grid    point   of
model  can  be  calculated by the given     external   force   condition   (
-144 -



open  boundary  condition ) such   as   tide,   discharge,   wind   etc   at
every computation time step.
At   this    moment,    advection    term     by    the    method    of
characteristics, diffusion and transfer force by the implicit finite
difference  scheme,   propagration    surface   and   seabed  friction   and
continuous  equation  by ADI    method ( iterative   alternating   direction
implicit  scheme )   can   be   solved   using  time    splitting   operator
technique. Flow  chart  for  the  computation   of  current   flow modeling
is described in Fig. 5. 1. 4 - 13.

Merits of K - cythere program are as follows.
<1>  Separation  of  non - linear   advection   by   the   method   of
characteristics  has  brought  the   improvement   of   irregular  vibration
of discharge and numerical damping.
<2>  By  using   the   iterative   alternating   direction    implicit
scheme  for  the calculation of    propagation.    precise   and  reasonable
results  without  significant    errors   even   in   the   case  of   large
scaled time step can be obtained.
(3> To simulate the actual condition more precisely, discharge
correction technique has been applied for tidal land to be exposed
at low tide.
<4> Variable grid mesh system is available.
b) Application of the Model.
1) Grid Mesh Composition
Grid  mesh  composition   in wide  area model    for  this   project
has the 114 km wide area in east - west dir.( X - axis ) and 146 km
wide  area  in  south - north   dir.( Y -  axis  )   from   the  center   of
project  site.  Grid  mesh   has  71 grid  lines  along X - axis    and   83
grid  lines  along  Y - axis,  totally   5,893  grid points.   By   adopting
the  variable  grid  mesh  system,   grid spacing  is one - half    nautical
mile  near  and  at  the   boundary   area   of   detail   model   and   one
nautical mile for other area.
Detail model has  the  41 km  wide  area   in east - west   dir.(  X-
axis ) and   30 km  wide  area   in  south - north  dir.(Y -axis  ).    Grid
mesh  compositions  are   77  grid  lines   along   X-axis   and   65   grid
lines  along  Y - axis,  totally  5005  grid points. ( See   Fig. 5. 1. 4  -
16 )     Mimimal  grid  spacing  has  been   fixed  to  200  m   at  Incheon
LNG  receiving terminal   area  and  entry of   sea  lane,   at   the  other
area grid spacing is larger. ( See Fig 5. 1. 4 - 18 )
(Table5.1.4-17 )              Wide Area Grid System

1 - 33          1,853.0                1 -  41       1,853.0 m
33 - 55            926.5              41 -   52        926.5
55 - 71          1,853.0              52 -   83       1,853.0

- 152 -



c) Calibration of the Model ( Simulation of the present state )
1) Calibration Period
Calibration  period  of    the   model   has   been   done   at  mean
spring  tide,  transient   state  which  can  be  estimated by M2   and    S2
component  tide   added  to  the  value  from  hourly observed  tide    level
data  during   30  days  at  Daeboo  island (1990. 11. 23 -  12.  22   )   by
harmonic  analysis.     Tidal  characteristics  at  Dae - boo    island   are
described at table 5. 1. 4 - 20 as below
( Table 5.1.4-20 )       tidal characteristic of daeboo island
Description      Observed results            Reference tide of Incheon
observed period     1990.11.23 - 12.22                1943 - 1944
H.W.O .S.T             863.3 m                        862.4 m
M.S.L               463.2                           463.5
L.W.O.S.T              63.1                            64.6
Spring range            800.2                          797.8
mean range              565.1                          572.4
neap range             329.9                          347.0
2) Opened Boundary Condition
- Wide Area Model
The  inputs  of  tide   condition  of  the  opened boundary  at   the
west  and  the   south,  discharge  condition  of Han,  Limjin  and    Yesung
river will be made at every 300 second computation time step.
Tidal   boundary    condition   has   been    derived    from    the
established   investigation  and  experimental   data,   calibrated  several
times  to  coincide   observed  tide  and  tidal  current  and  results    of
the modeling by the iteration.
- 153 -



- Detail Model
The  inputs  of  tidal  condition  at  the  south,   west and   north
the  three  directional  open   boundary   will   be   made  at  every   200
second  computation  time  step.   Tidal   boundary   condition   has   been
figured  out  and inputted  based on    the  calibration  results  of   wide
area  model, performed  calibration   test  sereral  times  till   coincides
observed tide  and  tidal   current  and  results   of   the   modeling   by
modifying tidal boundary condition.
3) Physical Parameter
- Computation Time Step
Computation time step shall satisfy Courant's stability equation
about  the  propagation  of    tidal   wave   and  stability   equation   is
presented as below.
CR =At v      -H /As ( 20
Where ; Cr = Courant number
At = Computation   time  step
As = Grid   spacing
g = gravity acceleration
H = Water depth
300  second  of    t  for  wide  area  model  and   200 see,   of    t
for  detail  model  has  been   utilized  to  satisfy  above condition   for
this project.
- Transfer Force
IUj=    U2 +      2
Strickler  parameter(k)   is computed   from    Strickler's  empirical
formula which is being used universally as below.
1   21.3
k = -=
n    d1/6
-134 -



Where, n = Manning's roughness coefficient
d = Grain size of sea bed sediment(mm)
Therefere, Strickler parameter can be calculated if grain size
of  the  sediment   is  given. Bottom  materials  of  site area mostly   are
composed of the sandy sediments and bottom friction coefficient of
the whole site is k = 50.
4) Calibration Result of Model
- Wide Area Model
Calibration  results  on observed   data  at   site   and the    value
from the modeling analysis indicates that tide is consistent almost
as  table  5. 1. 4 - 21  each   other    and   tidal  current   using   data
observed continuously has descrepancy less than 25 % as table 5. 1.
4 - 22, therefore sophisticated calibration analysis has performed in
conclusion. ( Table 5. 1. 4 - 21 and 22 )

d) Simulation
Simulation on   tidal  current   flow   has   been  carried   out   to
understand tide variation at open boundary of detail model by using
wide area model first, and based on above results, detail model is
utilized secondly.
Simulation  conditions  are  the case   1   of  impact   due  to  this
project  only,   the   case   2   of   the   combination   impact of   this
project,  the  completion of   Shi-hwa  reclamation  project, Song   island
primary stage reclamation project, the case 3 of combination impact
due to this project, the completion of Shi-hwa reclamation project,
the  completion  of  Song   island   reclamationl   project   for   present
area.
- Tide
(a) The Completion of Project Site Reclamation (lst case)
Low  water  level  has  no  significant   difference   with   present
state. ( See Fig 5.1. 4 - 18 )     High  water  level   is   decreased   at
northern  area  of  entry   whereas   increas,   Variation of   rising  and
descending is less than 10cm (Fig. 5.1.4-19)
At St-2 which is located in front of the terminal, low water    level
rise about lem and high water level descent about 4cm.
Accordingly, tidal range is decreased by 5cm (0.6%) than that of the
present (Table 5.1.4-25)

(Fig . 5.1. 4-19)              High Water Level Variation (Case 1)



(b) Project Site, the Completion of Shi-Hwa Reclamation & Song island
primary Reclamation Project (case 2).
L.W.L will be raised approximately 10 cm higher than the present state
at the whole area of detail model, however, maximum 15 cm higher between
LNG receiving terminal area and Shi-Hwa project site. (See Fig. 5.1.4-20)
H.W.L will be descend at the whole area of detail model, the more
closer to the beach, the higher descending height would be shown. (See
Fig.5.1.4-21)     Namely, descending height will be within   10  cm  between
Dae-moo-ui island and Hong island, 10cm - 15cm descended at the area from
Young-heung island pass by LNG receiving terminal to Incheon harbour,
15cm-20cm  descended  between  LNG  receiving  terminal   area  and   Si-hwa
reclamation area.
The reason why tide range is reduced is that tidal discharge is reduced
a lot due to the large scale reclamation through the hydrography between
Dae-Moo-Ui island and Young-Heung island and Incheon.
At St.T-2 in front of LNG receiving terminal area, total tidal range
will be reduced as much as 26cm (3.2%), in addition, 9cm ascended at L.W.L
and 17cm descended at H.W.L.
(c) Project Site and The Completion of Shi-Hwa and Song island Area
Reclamation (Case 3)
L.W.L  will  be  ascended  at  the  whole   area  of  detail   model,
distribution and ascending height are very similar to the Case 2. (Fig.
5.1.4-22).     Also H.W.L will be descended at the   whole  area  of  detail
model similarly like Case 2, but having 2cm-3cm drop more than Case 2.
(Fig. 5.1.4-23)   At St.T-2 in front of  LNG   terminal  area,  total  tidal
range will be reduced as much as 28cm (3.5%), in other words, 9cm ascended
at L.W.L and 19cm descended at H.W.L.

(Fig. 5.1.4-23)                  High Water Level Variation (Case 3)



Discharge of Tide
Discharge of tide which is the quantity of seawater passing through
the certain section of hydrography for one-tide period, can be fluctuated
due to reclamation, dredge etc, and variation of the discharge as above
would be the primary element which can create the change    of  tide   level,
velocity and reciprocation of sea water.       Tidal discharge which move  to
the direction of flood tide is not in accordance with that of ebb tide very
frequently for a tidal period, since the tide is non-linear which is
originated from topographical factor, bottom ,friction, consitent flow etc,
and former is called flood tide discharge, the latter is ebb tide
discharge.
At three sections which comprise the way to project site, section
between Young- heung and Dae-boo island (S-1), section between Young-heung
and Dae -moo ui island (S-2), and section between Young-jong island and
Incheon harbour(S-3), tidal discharge fluctuation has been investigated and
resulted in table 5.1.4-26.
( Table 5.1.4-26 )         Tidal discharge at each case
(Unit: lO6nit)
Present           Case 1          Case  2         Case  3

de chsch- dishrede disch- dshrede disch- de dis- de disch- dlischiarge
arge    discharge arge    di5chaige arge  charge arge
s- 1        58       9q     58       94      51      56     49       53
(0)    (-2)     (-7)   (-40)   (-9)    (-43)
S- 2     3,674    3,512   3,558   3,409    2,731   2,635  2,652    2,550
(-116)  (--309)  (-943)  (-877) (-1,022)  (-962)
S- 3
291      178    314     211      372     288     385     293
(+23)   (+33)    (+81)  (+110)  (+94)   (+115)
(1) Case 1
There is no big difference at St.S-1 with present state.At St.S-2,
average discharge at flood and ebb tide of present state has reduced as
much as 109 x 106le   from 3,593 x lO6 n  , while  at  St.S-3,  increased  as
much as 28 x 106 ,,  (12%) from 235 x 106 ,e
-165 -



(2) Case 2
Reduced discharge is as much as 23 x 106lo   (42%) from 77 x IO' n  at
present, state of St.S-1, 910 x 106 n   (25%) from 3593 x 106 n  at  present
state of St.S-2, while at St. S-3, 95 x 106 n     (40%)  discharge  will  be
added to 235 x 106n7  of present discharge.
The reason why a great reduction happens at St.S-1 and S-2 is the
decrease in reservoir due to the reclamation of Shi-Hwa and Songdo
project.In the meanwhile, a partial discharge lost their hydrography flows
into the front hydrography of Incheon and have the discharge of St.S-3
increased a lot. Discharge reduction could be the main reason which can
decrease the tidal range as described previously.
(3) Case 3
Variation of case 3 is very similar to that of Case 2 and the ranges
are a little higher than Case 2.      At St.S-I, discharge is decreased   as
much as 26 x 1O6 n   (34%) and 992 x 106ne  (28%) at St.S-2, while increased
as much as 105 x 106 ne  (45%) at St.S-3.
-   Tide  Velocity
(1) Case 1
Area where shows the increased tide velocity is the hydrographic way
of the front of Incheon and between LNG    receiving   terminal  and  Daeboo
island. At hydrographic way between  LNG  receiving    terminal  and  Daeboo
island, tide velocity can be increased as 10 cm/sec because the width of
way is greatly decreased  due   to  the  construction  of  causeway.   (Fig.
5.1.4-24).
At the front of Incheon harbor, average tide velocity is increased
not greater than 10 cm/sec according to the discharge increase, while the
tide velocity is decreased at the northern part of LNG receiving terminal
and southern part of entry road in all aspects.
Differences from the present state are not found at the entry and
turning area as a whole and at St.SC-11, maximum velocity at ebb tide is
increased as much as 17 cm/sec, from 95 cm/sec to 112 cm/sec (Table
5.1.4-27).
-166-



(2) Case 2
Tide velocity will be decreased at the whole area of    detail   model
except the front of Incheon harbour.   (Table 5.1.4-25)       At St.C-1, the
entrance area of LNG receiving terminal, present max. velocity at flood
and ebb tide are 94 cm/sec and 96 cm/sec respectively and will be decreased
18 cm/sec (19%) and 15 cm/sec (16%), either. At turning area, St.SC-10,
max. velocity shows a great reduction of 40 cm/sec where original was about
100 cm/sec.
In the meanwhile, at St.SC-1, present max. velocity of flood and ebb
tide are 78 cm/sec and 68 cm/sec, will be increased 16 cm/sec (21%) and 31
cm/sec (46%),either.
(3) Case 3
The Phenomenon to decrease the velocity to compare with the present
state is very similar to that of Case 2 except the increase of tide
velocity at the front of Incheon harbour and the variation is a little
higher than Case 2. (Table 5.1.4-26)
At St.C-1, maximum present tide velocity at flood and ebb tide are
94 cm/sec and 96 cm/sec respectively and reduced as 20 cm/sec (21%) and 17
cm/sec (18%).    At St.SC-10, turning area,   max.  tide  velocity  will  be
reduced as much as 35 cm/sec greatly from 100 cm/sec of the present.      On
the other hand, at SC-1, max. tide velocity of the present at flood and ebb
tide are 78 cm/sec and 68 cm/sec, however, increased as much as 20 cm/sec
(26%) and 34 cm/sec (50%) respectively.
-167-

2.   Numerical Modeling on Sedimentation
A) Outline of Modeling
1) Description of Experiment
Sedimentation in a semi-closed inner harbour like the site is
divided into bed load which is caused by the shear stress of current at
bottom and suspended solid caused by mud sediments repeating resuspension
and sedimenation.     Also, sliding and slumping could be created   at  the
slope surface such as dredged sealane by the current tide velocity or the
vibration due to ship transportation.   Water depth at this  area  is over
lOm, in excess of critical depth of drift movement and wave transferring
from the ocean can be protected mostly by the surrounded various islands,
therefore it is considered that sedimentation due to wave is negligible.
From the survey results on grain size analysis of bottom material for 10
stations, it is analyzed that sand over 0.063mm dia. are occupied 63% and
muds  less  than 0.063mm   dia.  are occupied   37%.     This  means   that
sedimentation by bed load is governing at this area but sedimentation by
suspended solid is still vigorous either.
Therefore, by using K-Cytengle modeling system to compute the
movement of bed load and the alteration of sea bottom by current velocity
and K-AMOSS program to solve the amount of sedimentation at each grid mesh
by analyzing equations about the sedimentation by suspended solid, the
total amount of sedimentation has been calculated on Case 1 and Case 3.
This analysis has carried out under the basic assumption that erosion and
sedimentation are depends absolutely on the bed load and suspended solid by
tidal current and sedimentations by wave, erosion and breaking of dredged
slope has not been considered.
2) Bed Load Sedimentation Modeling System (K-Cytengle)
K-Cytengle can calculate the movement of bed load, sedimentation due
to it and scouring depth by applying the current velocity and water level
computation  results of K-Cytengle  which  is   two-dimensional  sea water
fluctuation model. Basic equations are composed of formula for the bed load
movement, continuous equation and equation for correction and can be solved
by finite difference method.
-172-



(a) Formula for Bed Load Movement
Engelund-Hansen formular which used generally for the computation of
movement of sand sedimentation due to current flow has been applied.
T   =    1 - of g d~3. r0 6/2
here, T      Movement of Bed Load
f     roughness factor (= 1h 2g/V2)
A      Dry Density of Sediment particle
g     Gravity acceleration
d     Grain size of bottom material
Non-dimensional bottom friction (= hI/   d)
I     Energy slope (= V2 / K2 h4/3)
h     Water depth
V     current velocity
K     Strickler Friction coefficient
(b) Continuous Equation
Elevation of the sea bed can be extracted from the following equation
based on the calculation results of inflow or outflow discharge of bed
load.
+ div (mT) = 0
Where, Zb     : Height of Sea-bottom
div 7: Movement of Bed load (          +       )
ax      ay
m      : Extension factor
Where the computation of long term alteration of seabed is performed,
errors can be accumulated if final results are multiplied to one tidal
period in accordance with the pertinent period.      Therefore,  errors  have
been minimized by converting the results into pertinent period at every
time step and extension factor means the total number of computational
period.
-173-



(c) Correction Equation
In the case that the variation of seabed is serious, current tide
velocity can be affected by the change of water depth and the variation of
current velocity has included to increase the accuracy of test results.
Preconditions of correction are that the computed discharge from tidal
current modeling maintained without any correction at each grid   point  and
current velocity is propotional to water depth.
A (tt)
where,  V'      Current Velocity after correction
V       Current velocity before correction
h       Water depth
A Z     Height Variation of Sea-bottom
At      Computational time Step
3) Suspended Solid Sedimentation Program
K-AMOSS program have the capability to compute sedimentation rate of
suspended solid through semi-quantitative analysis by using suspended solid
characteristic   data  obtained   through  laboratory  analysis  of  in-situ
samples.       Current  velocity   and water   level,  which  are  the  most
important input, can be obtained from the analysis results of two
dimensional current modeling.
Neglecting the advection and vertical diffusion in other direction
(Y-dir) if current velocity in one direction (X-dir) is governed, then the
movement & diffusion equation of suspended load is as follows.
ac        ac       ac          a2c        a2c
+  U      - W      = - Dx .x- - D y
at        ax       az          ax2 
Where, C        Concentration of Suspended solid
W        Settling Velocity of Suspended solid
Dx, Dy   Diffusion coefficient in x,y direction
t       :Time
The solution of this equation by transforming the concentration (C) as
a function of time and space to the concentration (P) are as follows.
-174 -



p0                  w          CX-U(t-to)]2
p                    exp [--(t-tO)-
4 ,r v-D xD, t ~-t o 7   H 04DC(t-to)
yY2
4D,(t - to)
Where, U       : Average Current Velocity
H       : Water depth
0      : Coefficient of current velocity (= f(H, U*, a)
U*      : Frictional current velocity
a       : Water depth refered to concentration
RD (concentration rate of suspended solid in sea water) can be
obtained by integrating grid distance about x,y axis after passing some
time step,
RD =         EXP [-       (t-to) 
Where,  Mt     the amount of suspended solid at a time step t
Mo     initial amount of suspended solid
If  it  is  assumed  that  sedimented  suspended   solid  will  not  be
resuspended and the alteration of suspended solid at a time step t is
happened only by settling sedimentation,
then, SR will be
SR    1       = 1-EXP C-        Ct -to)
MO               H9 '
The amount of sedimentation at each section can be calculated by
multiplying the SR to the total amount of sedimentation of the whole
section area.        0   is as a function  of  water  depth,  current   tide
velocity and reference depth(a)    on vertical   distribution  of  suspended
solid, "a" is as same as roughness, can be obtained by the integration
about water depth assumming a/H = 1/20.
-175-



1  H C   a     H - Z  m  dz
H  a   H- a      Z
where   ; m     W/KU*
K     von Karman constant
U*    U * g/c
U     average current velocity
C     chezy constant ( = 18 log 10 (H/R))
R     roughness (m)
g     gravity acceleration (m/sec2)
Hence, DA at detailed each section can be computed by multiplying SR
at              each grid point to total amount of suspended  solid   at  the
whole area, considering that suspended solid   inflow   at  flood  tide   are
accumulated for approximately 6 hrs (a half tidal period).
DA = Mo x SR
Where,  Mo=   H x Ao x C
C  ; mean suspended solid concentration (ton/m3)
Ao ; Area (m2)
(a) Boundary Condition of Modeling
Sedimentation Test of Suspended Solid
(Table 5.1.4-28)     Sedirentation test condition of suspended Solid
t 1t 1 e                        Description
current velocity & water
Use analysis result of tidal current modeling
level
tide condition             mean spring tide
total computation time     one tidal period(12..5 hrs)
extension factor
-176-



- Sedimentation Test of Suspended Load
One of the important element which can affect on the sedimentation
analysis of suspended solid is the initial value of suspended solid
concentration.             Concentration of suspended  solid  is  controlled
largely under the tidal condition and wave statics and variable even in a
tidal period. In this test, sea water condition has divided into fixed
temperature condition and yellow spring condition, which is subdivided into
spring tide, mean tide,neap tide, initial value of suspended solid
concentration has been inputted as per each state in a fixed temperature
condition. (Table 5.1.4-29)
Based on the survey results of the concentration of suspended solid,
suspended solid is repeating resuspension and settling according to the
fluctuation of current velocity, thus it is very difficult to reflect the
behavior of suspended solid as above. Therefore, mean minimum value at
surface has been inputted as initial value on the assumption that it is not
resuspendable. (Table 5.1.4-29)
(Table 5.1.4-29)       Sedimentation test condition of suspended Solid
sea water condition   SS Concentration   settling velocity    period
spring tide             60               0.070             0.30
mean   tide            45                0.050            0.30
neap  tide             30                0. 350           0. 30
rough            80                0.090            0.10
Note:Period is a relative period hauing a year is unity.
(b) Modeling Results
By computing the cedimentation of bed load and suspended load, the
result on sedimentation and scouring depth per a year has shown on Figure
5.1.4-27 and Table 5.1.4.- 30.

- Present State
Sedimentation and scour occurred interchangeably, but sedimentation
area is more and especially sedimentation is governing at hydrographical
way in front of Incheon harbour.
- Case 1
Distribution of sedimentation and scour is very similar to the
present state and it is expected that sedimentations at southern and
nothern area of LNG receiving terminal will be increased a little more than
present. However, average SR is as exactly same as the present state of
1.2 cm/yr.     On the other hand, average SR are 0.7 cm/yr and 1.1 cm/yr at
entry and LNG receiving terminal area respectively, while they are smaller
than that of the whole  area.  ( Figure 5.1.4-29)
- Case 3
Distribution of sedimentation & scour is similar to the Case 1.
Average SR of the whole area is 1.2 cm/yr which is same as that of present
state and Case 1, 0.7 cm/yr at the entry and 1.2 cm/yr LNG terminal area,
which shows that they are similar to Case 1, either.                 (Table
5.1.4-31)

5.1.5 Natural Resources
A. Present Envrionment Condition
1. Agriculture
The numbers of househoLd in Incheon are 5,518 families, occupies only
1.28% of total 455,610 families of Incheon as of the end of 1,989 and
numbers of household totally engaged in agriculture are 2,540 families that
is 43.66% of the agricultural household, moreover only 0.56% of total
numbers of household.      In the meanwhile, farming populations are 26,113
persons and populations moved in agricultural household are 9,197 persons
which occupies 37.98% of    farming populations   and 0.57% of    1,754,376
persons of total population.
2. Foresty
Forest areas of Incheon city are classified as forest tree area of
6,893 ha and non-forest tree area of 207 ha, etc, totally 9,778 ha as of
the end of 1,989 which occupies 31.2% of total area of Incheon city, and
coniferous forest area in the forest tree area is 4,751 ha which holds
48.49% of total forest tree area and it indicates that coniferous trees
covers all over the forest area more than other trees.
3. Marine Products
Distribution of fishery in Incheon city as of 1989 are as follows.
Total 2,383 families of fishery houshold are composed of 1,966 household of
employer and 417 household of employee, which occupies 0.52% of total
numbers of Incheon house hold and fishery popalations are 9,909 persons
consist of 8,203 persons of employer and 1,706 persons of employee, occupies
0.56% of total  population.         On the contrary, fishery household  and
population are being decreased continuously 1% or so in a year.
-184 -



4. Mining and Manufacturing Industries
Numbers of mine per class in Incheon city as of   1989   are  33  mines
totally (20 of metal mine and 13 of non-metal mine) increased 20 no.s by
contrast with the numbers of mine(13) in 1988, however, actually only 20
mines are increased because non-operational mines are 26 places where
numbers of metal mine are 15 and of non-metal mines are 11.
Numbers of employees engaged in mine industries indicates 60.98% of
reduction, which is relatively high to compare with that of engineers and
administrative officer, it is considered due to the magnification and
automation of mines.
5. Fishery Rights
Marine resources at nearshore of Incheon are hair-tail, sepia
esculenta,  collichthys   niveatus,lmuraenesox   cinereus,  takifugu    sp.,
filefish, blue crab etc.,Also, there are some nurseries of meretrix
lusoria, cyclina sinensis and oyster, etc. the compensation on the damage
owing to the project construction has been completed while the process of
Shi-Hwa reclamation project and a fewnurseries 15 km far from the project
site are still remaining around Young-Jong island.
-185-

Incheon harbour to marine facilities,   400m  wide,  -13.965m     -18.6m of
variable water depth as required for the purpose of channel which goes to
11,859,000 e  totally and the entry road   7.5 km long,  8m wide   and  5.4m
high, will be constructed on the revetment which is linked from Dong-Choon
dong of Incheon and eastern part of project site.

5.2.2 Air Quality
A.   Present  Envrionment   Condition
To understand the status of air quality at project site, in-situ test
has been carried out Incheon, Shi-heung and Ong Jin koon where the impacts
are anticipated to exert due to this project and the test results will be
used for the simulation of air quality concentration in the future.
1. Review on the Existing Observed Data of Air Quality
Existing   data  near  project  site  presented   by  the  Ministry  of
Environment, observed at three automated station in Incheon as described in
Table 5.2.1-1.
(Table 5.2.2-1)   Location of Each Survey Site
Coordinates
City          Name                                   Location         Remarks
X (km)  Y (km)
Goo Wol Dong      174.31  428.90   176-2, Goo-Wol Dong,
Nam Koo, Incheon
Incheon   Soong Uei Dong    168.85   440.50  196, Soong-Yei Dong,
Nam Koo, Incheon
Boo Pyung Dong    175.85  444.20   442-1, Boo-Pyung Dong,
Nam Ku, Incheon
Reference: Emiromental Annual Book of Korea, 1990, Ministry of Environment
Results of air quality test by M.O.E.t shows that air pallutants are
ranged approximately as TSP 119-241 g/nd, SO2 0.013 - 0.174 ppm,NO, 0.016
- 0.037 ppm, CO 1.5 - 61 ppm, HC 2.2 - 3.0 ppm, 03 0.005 - 0.016 ppm and it
is investigated that TSP, SO2 are in excess of the standard of environment,
however, other such as NO,, CO, HC & 03 are near or less than the standard.
Above is expected to be caused due to complicated reasons like mass
population,transportation and operation of factories.

2. Survey on Air Pollution
a) Selection of Station
To find the status of air pollution at and near project site, five(5)
stations has been selected as table 5.2.2-9 & Fig. 5.2.2-1.
(Table 5.2.2-9)   Location and Reason of Selected Air Quality
Station                     Location                           Reason
A - 1     Wharf at Souttern Part of Incheon              To find Air Pollution
Harbour                                        Status near Project
Site
A - 2     0-i Island, Juenp-Joodong, Shi-Heung City,
Kychung-Ki Do
A - 3     In Front of Salterm, Koo Bong, Dae Boo
Myun, Ong-Jin Koon
A - 4     Rear of Pal-Mi Light House, Pal Mi Island
Moo-Ui Dong, Incheon
A - 5     Central of Project Site                        To Find Air Pollution
Status at Project Site
b)  Survey   Item  and  Analysis  Method of   Air  Pollution
Items to be surveyed for air pollution status are TSP, CO2, COD, NO2,
HC, 03, excerpted from 7 items of Basic environmental law, article 10 about
environmental standard, survey performed three times per station and the
sampling and analyzing method carried out on the basis of the law of
authorized air pollution test method as in table 5.2.2-10.

c) Survey Results of Air Pollution
To grasp the status of air pollution at and near project site, survey
has been performed Jan. 10-11, 1991 as the first, Mar. 29-30, 1991 as the
second, Jun. 6-7, 1991 as the third and the weather conditions at the date
on survey are described in table 5.2.2-11.
(Table 5.2.2-11)   Weather Condition on Survey Date

ture     dir.  (m/sec)         (%)

Survey results shows that TSP at southern area of Incheon port are
average 164.4   g/d, of    three  observation  in  excess  of  environmental
standard and at the project site, average of three observations are 68.7
g/m' of TSP, 0.022 ppm of So,, 0.014 ppm of NO2, 1.7 ppm of CO, 0.9 ppm    of
HC 0.003 ppm of 03 less than standard.
This is because the project site is located at offshore, hence sources
of air pollutants are not contained in the water and considered that
project site is under influence of the diffusion of air pollutants from the
circumference area of project site (Incheon, shi-heung, An-San).

3. Status Analysis by Modeling
To  grasp  the  concentration  of  air  polllution,   TCM-2  (   Texas
Climatoiogical Model - 2 ),a long term diffusin modeling,has been utilized.
a)   Background  for  Selection of   Model
TCM - 2 model has been selected through characteristics of the model
on air pollution diffusion and suitability analysis of project site and
principles & comparison on the modelings of air   pollution  diffusion   are
described in table 5.2.2-14 & 5.2.2-15.        TCM - 2 model  has  developed
and promoted by Texas Air Control Board in 1975 , which based on Briggs'
smokes diffusion  equation  revised   in  1980,Pasquill-Gifford's  diffusion
coefficient equation,  a half   period   equation  of  pollutants,  Gaussian
diffusion equation.         It is a climatological   model  to  predict  the
average concentration of non-reaction pollutants, utilized for the purpose
of analyzing on impact estimation of chimney & new pollutants, planning of
energy substitution, design of survey station, planing estimation & control
technology of air pollution, protection of sudden air pollution etc., and
aboves are the reason why TCM - 2 model has been chosen.
b)   Mathematical  fundamentals   of  modeling
Diffusion equation has been derived from Gaussian Plume equation and
average on-land concentration at landing point of K-th occurrence from
chimney can be calculated as below.
32 X 106Q I   0(K,m)                 H2
C (27)3'2 p  U*(HMm) zcm)   e x      2ai Cm)2 2
Where, C   Concentration (ug/m3)
0   Quantity of Pollutants (g/sec)
P   Distance from Stack to Setting point (m)
95 (K,M)  General Weather frequency function
K         Index of wind direction
m         Index of grade of air Stability
U*      : Average wind Velocity about stability grade at the   height
of Chimney
H         Effective height of the Chimney
az        Standard deviation   of  Concentration  distribution  about
verticai axis.

4. Computation of Pollutants Emission Amount
Pollutants emission amount has been computed by dividing as area, point
and line sources to perform modeling on the air quality status of project
site.
-221-



a)   Area  Sources
To trace the area sources at circumferencial area of project site,
project site have been consisted of each 1 sq. km grid area and calculate
numbers of households per each grid area by refering to statistical year
book & administrative district map of Incheon. Also, pollutants emission
per household has been excerpted from Environmental year book of Korea "
pollutant emission by the consumption of heating fuel in Incheon " and
seasonal pollutant emission are excerpted    from  Energy  Sensus  report
composition ratio of seasonal fuel consumption ".
(Table 5.2.2-16)   Pollutant Emission Per Household in Incheon City
(Unit: ton/year)
City       Household               TSP
Per year    Per household     Per year   Per household
Incheon      455,610       4,969          0.0109         14,541       0.0319
Reference: Environmental annual book of Korea, 1990, Ministry of Environment
(Table 5.2.2-17)   Seasonal Pollutant Emission per Household
(Unit: g/sec)
Description   Per year    Spring   Summer   Autumn    Winter       Remarks
TSP          0.0003    0.0004    0.0001   0.0003    0.0006
So2          0.0010    0.0012    0.0002   0.0007    0.0019
(Table 5.2.2-18)   Composition Percent of Seasonal fuel Consumption
Description     Spring        Summer       Autumn       Winter     Remarks
Composition     30.14         4.34         18.28        47.24
Percent
Reference: Energy Sensus Report of 1985, the Ministry of Energy Resources
Accordingly, analysis results by using the seasonal pollutant emission
as in the table 5.2.2 - 17 shows that total pollutant emissions are 1.8693
g/sec of TSP and 6.2310 g/sec of SO2 annually.

Y = a + bx
where; Y = corrected concentration
x = modeled concentration
a,b = parameter

(Ey) (EX2) -(X )       EXy)
a      N (EX 2 )  ((-C X)2
N C EXY)-(EX ) (EY)
b =
N ( EX2 )-   X2 )
where, N = no.s of station

x = computed concentration

observed and analyzed value.
E(qy_ y)2
where, Y = corrected concentration
Y = observed average concentration
Y = observed concentration
r = coefficient of corelation
s = standard deviation

B.   Environmental   Impact  by  Project
Impact on air quality due to this project can be divided largely into
a short term & long term impact and a short term impact would be generated
by the commited construction equipments & mobile transportation for
preparation work of LNG terminal site, for example, LNG reservoir tank,
evaporation  facilities,   appurtenances    etc.,to   be   installed   after
completion of project and harbour & marine facilities to be used for
loading/unloading of LNG.
However, in this estimation, impact due to pollutant emission by
heating for laboratory facilities & administration building only, since
contamination sources are not contained in above facilities and even in
loading unloading of LNG.
1.   During  Construction
A short term impact owing to site preparation, which is the major
impact element on air qaulity during construction progress, has been
considered.     Considered major pollutants within construction period    in
this  analysis   are  confined  to TSP    generated  from  the construction
equipment transportion & heaping and TSP, SO2, NO2, CO emited from fuel gas
used for construction equipment.
a)   Selection  of  Prediction  Method
For analysis of impact on air qaulity, TEM model in UNAMAP has been
utilized based on fundamentals of " Guideline on Air Qaulity Models, 1985 "
of EPA , USA. Characteristics of above model are as follows. ( table 5.2.2
- 31 )
-259-



(Table 5.2.2-31)   Fundamentals and Principales of TEM Model

Usage                    o Chimney Design
o Contamination Source Trace
o Study of Fuel Coefficient
o Study on Mitigation Measures of Air Pollution
Characteristic           Analyze a Short Term Concentration
Used Theory              o Steady State Shape Gaussian Plume Equation
o Briggs Dispersion Equation
o Pasquil-Gifford Dispersion Theory
Basic Equation           X(x,y,Q,H)  =  QX 106   exp (- (Y )2)exp
7 r  ' Y.JU      Qy
(-½ 2 ( H   2)
Where, Q     Pollutant Emission (g/sec)
U    Average Wind Speed (m/sec)
6Y6z: Horizontal & Vertical Dispersion Coeffi-
cient (m)
H : Effective Height of Chimney     (m)
b) Pollutant Emission of Construction Equipment
This LNG receiving terminal construction project can be divided into
causeway, revetment construction, dredging, reclamation, marine facility as
decribed in table 5.2.2 - 32 and construction progress schedule as
presented in table 5.2.2 - 33 shows that all kinds of construction work are
performed in Jun. 1992, thus pollutant prediction has    been  copmputed    by
assuming the case that all construction equipments are involved in the
site.

e)   Air  Quality   Prediction  during  Consruction
1)   Input  Condition
By utilizing the data of Incheon meteorological station, WNW of main
wind direction, 3.5 m/sec of wind speed, 11.4 C of average air temperature
are filled up as input condition for analyse air pollution due to vehicle &
equipment operation. In addition, 1,340 m of mixed height from the
observed radio sound data at Seoul has been also inputted.
Rocky mountain, Gathering & trnsportation route etc., around project
site has been filled up as area sources for analysis.
2)   Prediction   Results  of  Air  Quality
Impact analysis by TEM, a short term dispersion model, has been
carried   out to predict effects due to emitted pollutants and the    results
shows that 290.0 ug/sec of TSP, 6.22 ppb of SO2, 237.96 ppb of NO2, 42.58
ppb of CO are emitted and in the condition of weighing to present
concentration, then pollutants emissions are increased to 358.7 ug/sec of
TSP, 28.22 ppb of S02, 251.96 ppb of NO2, 1742.58 ppb of CO and therefore
analysis results shows that so2 & CO are anticipated   below  the  standards
except TSP & NO,.
-270-



Therefore, it is requested that mitigation measures,for example
adjustment of construction equipment, for TSP & N02 over the standards are
to be established based on environmenntal preservation law for air,
regulation of flying dust clause 28. ( table 5.2.2 - 41 )

2.   A  Long  Term Impact  Analysis  during  Terminal Operation
a)   Fixed  Sources
Facilities to be installed after the completion of this project are
LNG reservoir tank, evaporation facility, appurtenances & marine facilities
to be used for LNG loading operation and no particular air pollutants are
exist except appurtenances.
Accordingly, by applying " reasonable usage    standard  of  energy
issued from the Ministry of Construction no.646 ( 1986,10,16 ), pollutant
emissions   caused  by heating   of  laboratory  building,   administrative
building and exhibition hall has been computed.
applied equation
QA    QMAY X 24 X QY X (0.45 - 0.01 X F )
QA      A X (20-ti ) X 1,000
where, Qa     yearly heat load per unit area ( Mcal/n /yr )
Qmax   max. heat load ( Kcal/hr )
Qy     yearly heating day ( °C day )
F      no. of storey of building
A      heating area ( ne )
ti     outside temperature ( IC )
Hence, max. heat load can obtained as follows.
QA  X   A   X   (  20-t1   ) X   1,000  ... ........................  (2)
QY X 24 X ( 0.45 - 0.01 X F
Max. heat load has been predicted by Eq.2 applying -9.4°C as outside
temperature in air for heating system design, 3,250 C .day of class I area
for heating  day of referenced year, 60 Mcal/n .yr of class I area    below
5 storey for yearly heat load upper limit, since the site is located at
common water of Incheon city. likewise, energy amount used is calculated
applying 9,500 Kcal/nt of calorification , because LNG    is   planned   to
be consumed.
Resulted heat load by above is 6,389,753 Kcal/hr in a year and energy
to be consumed is presummed 672.6 ni/hr accordingly.

mainly.

C. Methods   for Reducing   tlre Baneful  Impact
Mitigation plan on impact of air quality ovwing to this project can be
divided into two Main cases, one is within construction period and the
other is after the completion of construction.
1. Air Quality during Construction
It is expected that fugitive dust will be generated due to cargo
transportation and heaving of earth, therefore, to control fugitive dust
generation based on the article 28 ( dust dispersion regulation ) of "
Environmental Preservation Law ", earth transportation cargo   shall  carry
excavated earth by perfect covering on it and washing a cargo & tires shall
be carried out before moving and perform water sprinkling on the road in
order to prevent contamination of  main transportation   roads and    speed
limit in the construction site will be not more than 10-20 km/hr.
< Tire washing facilities >
* width of water tank : more than 1.5 X length of cargo truck
* depth of water tank : more than 20 cm
$ length of water tank : more than 2.0 X length of cargo truck
* cleaness of water tank : install an equipment circulate clear water
to maintain turbidity below grade 10
* Install an equipment reciprocate polluted water in tank over
grade 10 of turbidity
* Permit admission only after cleanig dust on tires by round runnig
more than 3 times in a water tankf
< Car washing facilities >
* Sprinkling is possible to get reach from tire to top of cargo.
* Automatic or semi-automatic sprinkling equipment shall be installed
at both side
* hydropressure shall not be less than 10 kg/cm2
* Start to transportation only after clean particulates on tire &
a car perfectly by stopping more than 3 min.
* More than 5 degree of slope shall be maintained to guarantee free
passage of sprinkled water for washing
* For filtration of sprinkled water used for washing, appropriate
facilities shall be constructed for operation.
And then effective percent of dispersed particulate removal on unpaved
roads are summarized in table 5.2.2 - 52.

Also, when   particle   material   unloading   on   unloading   station

2.   After  Completion of   Project
There is no specific facilities to emit particular pollutants under
operation, impact due to heating of appurtenance facilities are to be
considered negligible and to mitigate pollutant generation during cooking
energy combustion processing or by mobile transportation, it is desirable
that planting trees on green tract of land & street having higher adorption
capacity and strong enough to resist sulphuric oxide and exhaust gas of
automobile to purify air pollution.

5.2.3 Water Environment
A. Present Environment Condition
1.   Sea- Water  QuaLity
a) Description
The project is to construct LNG receiving terminals by reclamating
tidal land   area of 1,200 m * 825 m in front of Song Do of Incheon    city,
and the site is not affected by waves from the ocean because it is
surrounded by various   kinds  of   islands  such  as    Young-jong  island,
Young-you island, Moo-uei island, Pal-mi island at northeast area and
Dae-boo island, Young-heung island, Kye-wol island, etc at southwest area.
Moreover, water depth at project site ranges about 2 m of tidal land,    and
current flow velocity at the main hydrographical way of entry to Incheon
harbour is 3 - 4 knots, 1.3 m/sec at flood tide   and  2.0  m/sec    at  ebb
tide.
On the other hands, seawater quality   standards  of  Incheon  coastal
area     are administrated and divided into three catagories like class   I,
II & III and water quality of project site shall be met class I standards
as shown at Fig.5.2.3- 1.

b)   State  of   Art  Investigation
Water quality investigation for Environtal impact analysis of common
water reclamation project adjacent to Incheon coastal area has been
carried out at Nov. 1989 & Feb. 1990 twice about seawater at surface &
bottom of ten (10) stations as shown Fig. 5.2.3 - 2 and analyzed as sea
water quality of class II for this area by detecting 7.8 - 7.9    mg/l    of
DO, 2.4 - 2.7 mg/l of COD, 20.1 - 22.2 mg/I of SS at station SWR-9
escribed in table 5.2.3 - 3.4 as below.
However, sea water classification of project site on the basis   of
Environmental annual book from the Ministry of Environment is presented as
class I quality by detecting 7.8 mg/l of DO, 1.0 mg/I of COD, 15.3 mg/l of
SS as shown in table 5.2.3 - 2.

c) Seawater Quality Survey
Stations for seawater quaLity to be observed has been taken at tidal
land appears above sea water level at low tide as shown at Fig.5.2.3-2
considering tidal current flow and survey carried out three times    winter,
spring, summer.
(Table 5.2.3-4)   Seawater Quality Survey Period
Survey Number                    Survey Date                  Remarks
1St                       1990.1.10-1.11                 Spring Tide
2Nd                       1990.3.29-3.30                 Neap Tide
3Rd                       1990.6.6-6.7                   Spring Tide
(1) Sampling and Analysis Method
Sea water sampling has been performed and obtained at upper & lower
layer utilizing submerged pump based on " Authorized test method of
Environmental pollution law for water pollution ( paragraph 1 sampling
method of chapter 2 generalized test method ), and reserve taken sea water
in sampler case which washed by 10 % nitric acid solution on the basis of
above law and tested at laboratory.

PH                   Survey at Site
Temp
And samples are analyzed based on the items becomes important
indications of environmental pollutions as follows.
i. water temperature
Surveyed at the site by DO meter ( YSI # 58 )
ii. pH
Surveyed at the site by pH meter ( ORION EA 940 )
iii. transparency
Surveyed at the site by 30 cm dia. secchi disk.
iv.   salinity & electric conductivity
Surveyed at the site by S-C-T meter ( YSI# 33 ).
v.    dissolved oxygen
Surveyed at the site by DO meter ( YSI # 58 )
- 303 -



vi.    COD
Standard mathod( EPA)
vii. total suspended solid
After filtration by standard glass fiber filter, dehydration
for 2 hrs. at 105°C and eruption & cooling at dethyeator, determined total
SS by      the difference of weight before & after test. ( Standard   method
of total SS test method )
viii.   Fixed suspended solid after heating
After complete total SS test, FSS has been estimated by the
weight difference using heating glass fiber filter at 550°C for 2 hrs.
ix.   volatile  suspened  solid
Can be solved by subtracting residual SS from total SS.
( Standard method of volatile SS test method )
x. nutrient salts
- total nitrogen
total nitrogen is the sum of ammoniac nitrogen, nitrous nitrogen and
nitric nitrogen.
- ammoniac nitrogen
Indian phenol method in light absorption intensity method
- Ammoniac Nitrogen
Investigated absorbance of blue colour of Indian phenol created by
reacting Ammmonium ion with phenol under coexistence of Chlorous acid
at 640 nm based on Indian Phenol Method from Absorption Photometry with
UV 2100S, Shimadzu. ( Ammoniac Nitrogen Test Method from Authorized
Environmental Pollution Test Method )
- Nitrous Nitrogen
Have Nitrous acid ion diazotization by reacting with Sulfonyl Amide
and investigated absorbance of red colour of coupling created by the
reaction with Alpha-Naphthalenediammine Chlorite at 540 nm based on
Ebrall-Norris  Method  from  Absorption Photometry   with   UV    2100S,
Shimadzu. ( Nitrous Nitrgen Test Method from Authorized Environmental
Pollution Test Method )
-304-



- Nitric Nitrogen
Based on Cd-Copper Reduction Method from Absorption Photometry,
efflux seawater on Cd-Copper column for reduction to Nitrous Nitrogen
and investigate the total amount of created Nitrous Nitrogen and
therefore, measure the amount of Nitric Nitrogen by reducing that
subtract initial amount of Nitrous Nitrogen from total amount of
Nitrous Nitrogen. ( Nitric Nitrogen Test Method from Authorized
Environmental Pollution 'Test Method )
- Phosphatic Phosphorus
Have Phosphoric acid ion react with Molybdenum acid and reduce
created Molibdenite acid phosphorus ammonium into tin chlorate by above
reaction and investigate absorbance with UV 2100 S, Shimadzu at 690 nm
based on tin chlorate reducing method from Absorption Photometry. ( tin
chlorate reducing method from Authorized Environmental Pollution Test
Method )
11. Total Alkalinity
By using PH meter ( ORION EA 940 ), it has been presented as
equivalence water CaCO3 which required for titration to pH 4.5 ( Total
Alkalinity Test Method from Standard Methods ).
12. Heavy Metals
Sampled seawater has been quantified by DDTC -   MIBK extraction   from
Authorized Environmental Pollution Test Method.
Take 250 ml sample at 500 ml separatory  funnel  and neutralize until
yellow color turns to green color by adding 2 or 3 drops of Citric acid
ammonium ( 25 w/v % ) and Brom thymol blue ethyl alcohol ( 0.1 w/v % )
and put Ammonia into it in addition.
And set the sample for 2 minutes after mix and addition of 40 X,
Sulfuric acid ammonium liquids 10 ml and DDTC ( 10 w/v % ).
Add MIBX 20 ml and set them for 30 minutes after heavy mix and mix MIBK
by heating at water bath after separating MIBK layer.
And transfer them into 25 ml Volumetric Flask cleaned by 1N - HNO3
several times after adding and heating concentration of HCI ( 1: 1 ) 10
ml.
Then after store them  in I-IDPE according  to   w M , calculate metal
concentration based on the calibration curve prepared by standard
solution of each metal by obtaining absorbance from the max. absorb
wave of each metal using AA ( Shimadzu, AA - 680 ).
- 305 -



- Cr +6 ; Perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric acid and
investigate using AA Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atomic Absorption
Photometry after total Chrome is changed to Cr6 by oxidation of
Permanganate Kalium. ( Cr"6 Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test
Method )
- Cd ; Invetigated using AA Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atcmic
Absorption Photometry after perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric
acid. ( Cadmium Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test Method )
- Pb ; Investigated using AA Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atomic
Absorption Photometry after perform priming by Nitric acid - perchloric
acid. ( Plumbum Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test Method )
- Cu ; Investigated using M    Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atomic
Absorption Photometry after perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric
acid. ( Copper Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test method )
-  Hg ; Perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric acid first of all
and investigate by evaporating Mercury solution through ventilation
after reduction to metal Mercury putting Sncl2.
Mercury hydride system and AA, Shimadzu AA - 680 has been utilized for
analysis. ( Mercury Test Method and Reducing vaporization circle Method
from Authorized Pollution Test Method )
- Zn ; Investigated using AA Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atomic
Absorption Photometry after perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric
acid. ( Zinc Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test Method )
- Al ; Investigated using AA Shimadzu AA - 680 based on Atomic
Absorption Photometry after perform priming by Nitric acid - Perchloric
acid. ( Aluminium Test Method from Authorized Pollution Test Method )
13. Specific Toxic material
- Oil particle ; Investigation method which obtain the value from the
weight of residual material, evaporate normal nucleic acid, which
extracted from normal nucleic acid after have Nlormal nucleic acid,
extracted from the sample, precipitate by precipitant and dissolve
precipitates by Chloric acid.     ( Oil  particle Test Method     from
Authorized Environmental Pollution Test method )
14. Colitis germs
MPN Test from Authorized Environmental Pollution Test Method has been
utilized.

circumfer-
encial area.

B.   Environmental   Impact  by  Project
Impact on shore area of Incheon due to this project could be divided
into    construction stage of dredging & reclamation and operation stage to
emit   polluted water, therefore   impact  analysis   has  been  carried  out
utilizing Dimos - II modeling in the consideration of above effects at
each stage.
1. Description of Model
Dimos - II modeling system is used for the computation of movement,
diffusion & periodical and spatial variation of SS & COD due to sea water
fluctuation as two dimensional model, and flow charts are shown at Fig.
5.2.3 - 4 and basic equation is presented as below.
u   aV     a8c      18a           ac      1     a       ac
at    Ax      ay    h     ax )              ax          a y
+     a   (h k21  ax ) +-     -     ( h k22 a-   ) + -
hay           ax       h   ay            ay      h
where,  x, y    two dimensional coordinate
t     :Time
h      Water Depth
c      Average Concentration of Pollutants
u, v   Average Current Velocity in x, y Direction
kil, k12, k21, k22 : Directional /durbulent Diffusion Coefficent
S      Extinction & Creation

Components of diffusion ( Fig. 5.2.3 - 5 ) can be taken from the trans
formation of stream line coordinates to two dimensional coordinates and
these are expressed as stream flow direction (d ) and normal  direction(  )
in equation as below.
kl=       cos2  + en sin2o
k 12    ee - e r ) coso sino
k22 =     sin2o + er cos20
where, eC, en     Mixed Coefficent in Flow Direction and Normal Direction
a        : Angles to & Axis From x - Axis  (Positive  in anti-clock
wise)
y
/ direction of
current speed
x
(Fig 5.2.3-5) turbulent flow diffusion coefficient calculation System
e e and e ' can be obtained by solving Elder's equation using
character-
istics of mean flow as follow.
e e  =   eL   u* h
en     =  eT  u* h
Where, eL and eT   are  non-dimensional  coefficient of   stream  flow
direction    and normal direction, 5.93 & 0.23  respectively  according  to
Elder's experiment and u* is current shear velocity and h is water depth.
However, difficulties in solving traditional numerical modeling are to
calculate &   simulate numerical damping ratio & irregular vibration caused
by applying   identical numerical solutions to advection of left  side  and
diffusion of   right side having different equation to  be solved   in  the
process of resol-
-314 -



ution of diffusion equation.   Therefore,  to grade up the accuracy     of
analysis and minimize numerical   errors in this modeling, complex behavior
such as movement   and diffusion     etc.,  of pollutants  are separately
calculated  for  this  analysis.    In other words,    advection  term   is
calculated by  solving  the positive      finite differential  method  and
diffusion term is calculated by solving the negative finite differential
method ( split operator algorithm ).
In  addition,  there exist   a technical   limit on  computation of
extinction   & generation of COD based on biological & chemical  activities
of  organism  considering  as   non-preservative   materials.   Therefore,
extinction ratio calculated by empirical equation as below is included in
the analysis.
Generally, COD extinction ratios are expressed according to time
variation as follows.
ac   =  -Kd-C
at
where,   C  : COD Concentration at any Time
Kd : Extinction Rate
Extinction ratio kd can be obtained approximately by following equation.
Log,, ( Kd H2 / v ) = -3.606 + 1.383 Log10 (H  `gH / v)
where, H     Water Oepth
v    Kinectic Viscos Coefficient of Sea-water (m2, sec-1)

(2) SS Concentration at the Outlet of Spillway
SS concentration at the outlet of spillway has been calculated by
empirical method of J.0.C ( Japan Ocean Company ). Thus, suspended solid
removal ratio in the settling reservoir can be predicted by the rising and
settling velocity of each soil particle diameter.
U ( rising velocity of soil particle ) =             0.0005 n/ nt * hr
A   L
where, U = rising velocity ( m/h )
Q = drainage ( nt/h )
A = width of settling reservoir ( m )
L = length of settling reservoir ( m )
( settling velocity of soil particle ) V = g(p8sU )-d
where, V = settling velocity
g = gravity acceleration
-320-



Removal ratio of soil particle can be divided into two cases
according        to rising velocity (U) as below.
- if    U < 0.05 n /d .h
R = 100 X 10( A.U**2 + B.U )
A   27.658 X log V - 25.726
B=   0.285 X log V - 0.289
where, R = percent of pollution & turbidity removal
V = mean settling velocity of soil particle
- if     U > 0.05   e /d .h
R   Al.log U + Bl
Al = 0.62( log V )2 + 38.97( log V ) - 37.51
Bi   0.97( log V )2 + 67.25( log V ) + 34.76
Hence, based on   empirical  formula,  unit  value    is  analyzed  that
removal of soil particle by dia. of bottom material    at  dredging  area   is
99.63 %   and SS concentration at the outlet of spillway    is  531  mg/l  as
presented in table 5.2.3- 14.

(3) Unit Value of Pollutant Emission due to Stone-Throwing

largely   dependent   upon  the  soil  contents,   diameter  distribution  of
contained    soil, how to drop etc., and unit value of pollutant   source  is
variable    to the size of earth transportation barge if   Grab  dredging  is
used.

under the process of dredging, reclamation of dredged soil, stone-throwing

to be 9 months, 11,859,000 7i for dredging proceess, 12 months, 1,233,0007e
of stone  for  causeway  construction  and  15 months,    1,113,000  7i  of
stone-throwing for revetment construction.

assessment data and required earth amount for construction, are evaluated
as   155.08 t/day in dredging process, 22.96 t/day in dredged soil process,

3.   Numerical  Modeling   on  Pollutant  Diffusion
a)    Condition  of  Modeling
For this modeling, SS diffusion has been evaluated under the
assumption that situations for SS emission can occur simultaneously during
the process of Incheon LNG receiving terminal   construction.   For  onshore
construction, SS is presummed to model 24hrs occurring in a day since
onshore construction work continues for 24 hrs and for    dredging works, SS
occurrence does not modeled for 9 hrs assuming 15 hrs working a day.
Conditions for modeling are presented in table 5.2.3 - 9 and SS occurrence
and location are also presented in table 5.2.3 - 20 and Fig. 5.2.3 - 6.

b)   Modeling  Results
1)    During  Construction
The most important elements having a decisive effect on the
movement,diffusion of SS caused by this project construction are velocity &
direction of tidal current.      In other words,  SS  moves  to  the  inland
coastal area at flood tide and  moves & diffuse to the ocean at ebb tide.
Therefore, among total 85 hrs test result for prescribed 3 cases,
the    last period analysis results which concentration variation   for  one
tidal period reaches to semi-normal condition has been utilized for
analysis, and especially, results at high water level and low water level
in contrast each other in concentration distribution of one tidal period
has been estimated very carefully.
(a) At High Water Level
Overall distribution of SS concentration increasement at each case
are similar one another. ( Fig. 5.2.3 - 7 thru 9 )     In other   words,  SS
will be diffused northwest to southeast direction    along the coastal  line
from the centerline of causeway, and   1 ppm     concentration  increasement
contour range reaches approximately 10 km, near Incheon harbour in
northwest direction to frontal of Ban-wol    city  in  southeast  direction.
The reason why diffsion range and concentration increasement of SS are
large comparatively is the shallow water depth at flood tide due   to   wide
tidal land develoment at this area.
On the other hands, since dredged sea lane having higher loads have
deep water depths & swift current velocity, SS concentration does not
increased that much regardless installation of silt protector,however,the
effect transfer to coastal area.
As it were, SS occurred at dredging process of sea lane ai-e moved &
diffused towards Ban-wol city via southern part of LNG receiving terminal
along     current flow, and case 1 ( without silt protector ) shows    wider
range   of concentration increasement than case 2 & 3 ( with silt protector
Area to increase over I ppm is 144.4  ,   in case 1, 129.9 ki  in  case
2 diminishes 10 % to  compare   with  case  1,  and  111.5  k    iLn  case  3
diminishes to 23 %.      Whereas areas to increase over 10 ppm is  37.2 da
in case 1, 35.9 kg      in case 2 decrease to 3 % to compare with   case  1,
and 32.0 1 dk in case 3 decrease to 14 %. ( table 5.2.3 - 21 )

C.   Methods  for   Reducing  the  Baneful  Impacts
1.   During  Construction
To mitigate pollution and turbidity of sea water quality due to the
project construction such as sea lane dredging, causeway & revetment
construction, following methods are introduced and used.
a)   Construction  of  Filter  Mat
To reduce pollution & turbidity caused by reclamation during
revetment     construction process, first   construct  quay  wall  and  then
reclaim dredged soil and earth inside it to mitigate occurrence of SS
maximally,   and   install  filter  mat  on  the  slopes  to  quarantine  SS
occurrence thoroughly.
By installing filter mat on the slope, it is expected that dredged
soil would not be of effluence and suction, improvement of   stability   can
be attained by lowering ground water level through amicable permeability,
the quality of marine environment   can  also  be  improved   by  precluding
pollutants emission such as SS through filtration.    Materials  for  filter
shall be 100 % Poly Propylene, Poly Etylene material which is endurable,
anti-acid, anti-alkaline and water tight.
Filter Mat

b)   Silt  Protector  Installation
It is planning to install silt protector to prevent pollutant
diffusion owing to earth dropping into the sea water for revetment & quay
wall construction at the location expected to be polluted, considering
local     characteristics.    Silt  protector  will  be employed   for  the
period of process of revetment & quaywall construction, dredging works.,
etc.
Generally, diameter of silt particle  is over   0.07    m,  thus  the
effluence of silt will be prevented almost perfectly because porosity of
silt protectors  is 0.04   m X 0.16   m.



- Selection of Silt Protector
i) Determine External Force
P X Co X V2
p=             ~~~CoS2Q
2 X g
where, P = calculated external force ( kg/m2 )
Co = drag coefficient
g = gravity acceleration ( m/sec2 )
p = weight density of sea water or air ( kg/m3 )
V = velocity of wind, wave or current ( m/sec )
Q = approaching angle of wind, wave or current
ii) Determine Tensile Force at Canvas
Po x a
2 X f
where, T = tensile force at canvas ( kg/m )
2a = anchor spacing ( m )
Po = resultant of external forces ( kg/m2 )
f = deformation ( m )
iii) Selection of Silt Protector Canvas
Select  canvas  material  which   has   a   suitable   factor   of
safety,considering a nature of construction work and a condition of
employment, on its yieid   strength  about determined tensile    forces  at
canvas.
- Silt Protector Installation Procedure
Consideration of marine environmental condition
Make an arrangement of mainanchor & subanchor after determination of
anchors
Transport silt protector & anchors by a large size barge
Connect by wire rope between anchor at sea bottom and lower part of
silt protector

2. Under Operation of LNG Receiving Terminal
It is expected that pollution of near area at LNG receiving terminal
will be minute, since 0.01 mg/l of COD will be added due to 16.5 nd of
sewage       quantity and 168 mg/l of BOD under operation of      LNG   receiving
terminal.
However, in this project, environmental impact will be more negligible
by contact stability method which can reduce BOD concentration to 25.2 mg/l
removing 85 % of effluence.( Fig. 5.2.3 - 15 )
Ao t ai antett er         tank                d
E~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Lsurplus sludge
t slud~gethi`ckner Sdisposal
(Fig 5.2.3-15)             sewage treatment diagram
Also, it is anticipated that water pollution due to sewage discharge
from vessels and oil discharge due to unexpected accident such as vessel
crashing can be happened because of marine life at & around LNG receiving
terminal.
Accordingly, sewage from the vessel will only be allowed to be
discharged    at the high sea area where does not affect due to pollution by
reserving sewage in the vessel temporarilly, and following equipments shall
be provided for oil discharge accident caused by emergency of vessels to
prevent sea water pollution.
- Oil Fence
Equipment for oil gathering and diffusion prevention is consist as
follows.
Flotation system : lave a enough buoyancy to resist any gravity loads
Freeboard : Oil integrated on it and not to overflow.
Skirt : Prevent oil pass through under oil fence.
Ballast : Keep oil fence in right position
Misc. : anchoring point, anchor, plates
- :341 -



Oil Skimmer
Generally, oil skimmer is used for the case that oil is sustained
certain depth of layer, in other words, the thicker the oil layer, the
easier to remove.    Reverse panel type which connect to  suction pump    is
used effectively
for the quite thick layer of oil.     With the exception of   above,  there
are a diffusive, an adsorbent and   a settler for chemical control.
5.2.4 Soil Pollution
A.   Present  Envrionment  Condition
1.    Existing Observed   Data  for  Soil  Pollution
Soil pollution is an indirect pollution that can affect not only to
a man feeding from the polluted crops but also to the growth of plants and
crops by accumulating organisms in it.
This means that plants are getting the most of nitrogens from the
excretion of bacteria, which cannot be obtained from the air, however, the
destruction of land ecosystem due to artificial pollutants adhered to soil
reaches to abnormal condition by changing the composition of soil, thus, it
interferes the growth of the crops & plants.
Soil pollutions are derived from the air & water pollution and
agricultural material such as agricultural chemicals, paint and the waste
disposal etc., and the process is as follows.
National average heavy metal concentration in 1989 is 6.1 mg/kg
of pH,     0.287 mg/kg of Cd, 11.687 mg/kg of Pb, 0.118 mg/kg of Hg,   7.209
mg/kg of Cu, 16.167 mg/kg of Zn, 0.627 mg/kg of as described as in the
table 5.2.4 - 1, whereas critical concentration of crops growth is 25 mg/kg
of Cd, 450 mg/kg of Pb, 45 mg/kg of Hg, 125 mg/kg of Cu, 3.25 mg/kg of Zn,
15 mg/kg of As shown as in table 5.2.4 - 2.

Analysis results on soil pollution as stated in table 5.2.4 - 6 shows

soil pollution observed.

5.2.5 Waste
A. Present Environment Condition
Wastes are the liquid, solid or semi-solid type material those are not
reusable for human life and economic activity any more, and they are major
problem nowadays in environment due to waste increasement in quantity and
variety in quality  by population    increase  & concentration   and   rapid
industrial development.
1. Refuse
a)   Status  of  Refuse Occurrence
To evaluate generally primary factors to increase refuse by analyzing
refuse production status of Incheon city, data from cleaning section of
Incheon city shows that special cleaning districts are 47 kd at Nam - koo
to which the project site belongs among the total 313 kX of administrative
district and 456,597  population   in  Nam  -   koo  among total   1,754,376
population in Incheon city.

b)   Refuse  Disposal  Method
Refuse collection is being done using 464 no.s of handcart and 4 no.s
of
heavy equipment by Incheon city itself, and using 806 no.s of handcart &
216 no.s of refuse vehicles by cleanig agency for refuse disposal as of
the end of 1989.
The types of refuse collection method being performed are manual
collection, truck collection & mass collection largely, hence, for places
where truck can easily acess truck collection system is being generally
used and then hauled to treatment facilities, and for commercial area &
places having irregular alley manual collection is performed, in other
words, primary collection is made by handcarts and gathered at intermediate
container box and then hauled to treatment system by vehicles.

B.   Environmental Impact  by  Project
Environmental pollution due to wastes can cause contamination of sea
water or another kind of pollution according to the process of treatment of
waste.
The purpose of land utility of this project is planning for LNG
receiv     ing terminal only, thus, wastes production will not be generated
due to land usage, however, it is expected that wastes will be produced
- 354 -



S
from operation crew of LNG receiving terminal and wastes from LNG carrier
tanker is considered negligible. Refuses produced from the site would
mostly be wastes in everyday life, for example, food wastes, paper wastes,
aluminium cans & glass bottle, etc.
Accordingly, refuse unit source value by the operation crew of Incheon
LNG receiving terminal has been computed from " Environmental annual book
of Korea, 1990, Ministry of Environment", excluding briquet.

o Operation crew of Incheon LNG receiving terminal
- for operation : 70 persons
- for maintenance : 85 persons
- for administration : 145 persons
- total : 300 persons
o Daily production quantity of wastes from living
- food wastes : 300 persons X 0.45 kg/day.person = 135 kg/day
- paper.wood wastes   300 person X 0.28 kg/day.person = 84 kg/day
- metal.glass wastes   300 person X 0.09 kg/day.person = 27 kg/day
- others : 300 person X 0.29 kg/day.person = 87 kg/day
- total wastes production   333 kg/day

paper wastes ( woods ), 27 kg/day ( 0.1 % ) of metal.glass  wastes   among
135 kg/day of total, and all these will be treated on consignment to
Incheon city.
5.2.6 Noise and Vibration
A. Present Environment Condition
Rapid industrial development has brought the  appearance of   various
kinds of machinery & tools and noise & vibration from those are increased
accordingly, thus, these noise & vibration are becoming major elements
lowering the quality
of life by causing sentimental instability, insufficient sleeping etc.
Major sources of noise and vibration in cities, in general, are traffic
noise & vibration produced by vehicles traffic, factory noise & vibration
produced by factory operation and construction noise & vibration produced
by construction site etc, and traffic noise & vibration are spreaded over
entire city whereas noise & vibration due to construction activity and
factory operation are local and transient.
On the other hands, the project site where is situated on tidal land
,appears above sea water level at L.W.L, has no specific noise sources,
however, present state has been observed and analyzed as follows to obtain
basic data for impact prediction on circumferencial area of project site
due to construction activity.
1. Noise
a) Location of Stations
Stations where are representative of each land utility has been
selected for three times observation by sources of noise, and location of
stations     are shown at table 5.2.6 - 1 & Fig. 5.2.6 - 1.
Analysis Period
